Indiana & Michigan Power Company v. Public Service Commission


Docket No. 59197


Supreme Court of Michigan


405 Mich. 400; 275 N.W.2d 450; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 331


December 9, 1977, Argued  
February 5, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 10, 1979, 406 Mich 1119.
Rehearing denied by Indiana & Michigan Power Co. v. PSC, 406 Mich. 1119, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 1569 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: 72 Mich App 398; 249 NW2d 429 (1976).
Indiana & Michigan Power Co. v. State, 72 Mich. App. 398, 249 N.W.2d 429, 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1104 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and commission, challenged the decision from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed a trial court's judgment granting a refund of a statutory issuance fee to appellee power company. The power company had paid the fee pursuant to appellants' mandate.


OVERVIEW: The power company filed certain applications with the commission seeking approval or a disclaimer of jurisdiction of certain planned security issuances. The commission approved the proposed transaction and ordered the power company to pay to the state the statutory fee. After it did so, the power company sought a refund of the security issuance fee and filed an action in the trial court. The trial court granted a refund to the power company, and appellants challenged the ruling. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. On further review, the court reversed and held that the commission properly exercised jurisdiction over the securities of the power company under Mich. Comp. Laws § 460.301 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 2.101). The court concluded that the securities regulation was intended to, and did, protect interests that rate regulation alone did not effectively control. The court concluded that the federal regulatory scheme applicable to the power company did not preempt state regulation of the power company's securities issuances.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment affirming the trial court's grant of a refund of a statutory issuance fee to the power company.

 

280 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nuss


Docket Nos. 59780, 59781


Supreme Court of Michigan


405 Mich. 437; 276 N.W.2d 448; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 333


March 7, 1978, Argued  
February 5, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 75 Mich App 346; 254 NW2d 883 (1977).
People v. Nuss, 75 Mich. App. 346, 254 N.W.2d 883, 1977 Mich. App. LEXIS 1109 (1977)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecutor appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed trial court denials of defendant's motions to quash the complaint and warrants charging defendant with first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: After confessing to two murders, defendant was confined to a state hospital pursuant to his petition under the Criminal Sexual Psychopath Act, Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.967(1)-(9) (1948). Contemporaneously with the filing of that petition, defendant also filed a demand for a speedy trial in one of the murder cases pending against him. No action was taken on that demand, and defendant was ultimately confined in a state hospital for approximately seven years. After defendant was released from confinement, the prosecutor charged him with the murders. Defendant filed motions to quash the complaints and warrants, alleging that they violated his state and Federal constitutional rights to a speedy trial and against double jeopardy and pleading the statutory bar to prosecution in § 8 of the Criminal Sexual Psychopath Act. The court affirmed a determination of the intermediate appellate court that § 8 of the Criminal Sexual Psychopath Act prohibited prosecution of defendant, and that his due process right not to be prejudiced by an inexcusable delay between the date of the murder for which he had demanded a speedy trial and the date of trial precluded prosecution for that murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court granting defendant's motions to quash the complaints and warrants charging him with first-degree murder was affirmed.

 

281 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Neumayer


Docket No. 59093


Supreme Court of Michigan


405 Mich. 341; 275 N.W.2d 230; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 329


June 6, 1978, Argued  
February 5, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 10, 1979, 406 Mich 1118.
Rehearing denied by People v. Neumayer, 406 Mich. 1118, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 1532 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Newmayer, 402 Mich. 802, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1317 (1977)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people appealed from the Michigan Court of Appeals, which denied leave to appeal the reversal of defendant's conviction on charges of dissemination of obscene materials in violation of the Michigan criminal obscenity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.343a. The lower court had reversed defendant's conviction on the ground that the statute did not apply to dissemination of obscene materials to consenting adults.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction under the Michigan criminal obscenity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.343a, was reversed because the lower court held that it applied only to distribution of obscene materials to juveniles, not to consenting adults. The people appealed and the court affirmed the reversal of the conviction, but then construed the statute to provide a constitutional prospective application as to adults. The court said that the language of the statute as written was unconstitutionally vague and thus did not give defendant notice that his conduct was prohibited at the time he committed the acts charged. However, the court said that the statute should be construed in a manner consistent with both the federal and state constitutions. The court adopted a three-part test and definitions established by the U.S. Supreme Court in Miller v. California, 413 U.S. 15 (1973), to provide the requisite degree of specificity and careful limits required of a statute to regulate speech among adults. The court joined other state courts in opting to "Miller-ize" their existing obscenity laws by judicial construction rather than declaring them unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the reversal of defendant's conviction because at the time of the acts charged the court had not construed the statute to proscribe such conduct. The court reversed the determination that the statute was unconstitutional, however, and applied a prospective construction which was consistent with the federal and state constitutional guarantees of free speech.

 

282 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Green


Docket No. 59674


Supreme Court of Michigan


405 Mich. 273; 274 N.W.2d 448; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 433


June 6, 1978, Argued  
January 26, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 74 Mich App 351; 253 NW2d 763 (1977).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. Prior to trial, defense counsel had unsuccessfully moved to suppress evidence of statements defendant made to an assistant prosecuting attorney and a detective outside of the presence of defendant's counsel on the ground that the prosecuting attorney violated Mich. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 7-104(A)(1). The Court of Appeals (Michigan) affirmed the conviction and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made the statements to the detective and the assistant prosecuting attorney after knowingly waiving his Miranda rights. He contended, however, that the statements should be suppressed because the assistant prosecuting attorney violated DR 7-104(A)(1). The appellate court found no error, holding that an ethics violation alone did not warrant or require the suppression of voluntary statements. The court upheld the conviction. The language of DR 7-104(A)(1) was clear and contained only two exceptions. It provided that a lawyer shall not communicate with a party he knows to be represented by a lawyer unless he has the prior consent of the lawyer representing that party or is authorized by law to do so. While a criminal defendant's initiative and willingness to speak with law enforcement authorities without his attorney and the lack of over-reaching by a prosecuting attorney were factors to be considered in mitigation, they did not excuse a prosecuting attorney's compliance with the standard of professional conduct prescribed by DR 7-104(A)(1). Nevertheless, disciplinary proceedings against the prosecuting attorney were the proper remedy, not suppression of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Dukesherer Farms, Inc v. Director of the Department of Agriculture (After Remand)


Docket No. 59321


Supreme Court of Michigan


405 Mich. 1; 273 N.W.2d 877; 432 N.W.2d 721; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 426


January 6, 1978, Argued  
January 9, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 73 Mich App 212; 251 NW2d 278 (1977).
Dukesherer Farms, Inc. v. Ball, 73 Mich. App. 212, 251 N.W.2d 278, 1977 Mich. App. LEXIS 1312 (1977)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cherry farmer challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which upheld a trial court's ruling that the Agricultural Commodities Marketing Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 290.651 et seq., was a permissible assessment, and not a tax, and therefore defendant, Director of the Department of Agriculture, could seek funds from plaintiff to use in the marketing of state grown cherries.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature passed the Agricultural Commodities Marketing Act (Act), Mich. Comp. Laws § 290.651 et seq., (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 12.94(12)) et seq., allowing the Director of the Department of Agriculture to seek funds from various farmers to market agriculture goods. Cherry farmer filed suit against the director, claiming that the Act was an illegal tax and an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority. The trial court and appellate court upheld the Act, and farmer sought further review. The court held that the Act did not place a tax upon farmers, but merely an assessment, because the funds generated did not benefits all the people of the state, but merely the growers of the agriculture products. The court also determined that the Act did not place legislative authority in the hands of the director, because he was acting merely pursuant to the dictates of the Act, and only acted with the authority vested in his position by the legislature. The court affirmed the lower court, and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, holding that state law allowing the director to place an assessment on agriculture growers for marketing purposes was not an illegal tax, nor was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority.

Workman v. Detroit Auto. Inter-Insurance Exchange


Docket No. 58106


Supreme Court of Michigan


404 Mich. 477; 274 N.W.2d 373; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 421


March 3, 1977, Argued  
January 4, 1979, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which determined the liability between defendant insurers and the set-offs available under the Michigan No-Fault Insurance Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3101 et seq., after plaintiff passenger sustained injuries from an accident. Plaintiff cross-appealed, filed a motion to reopen proofs, and filed an amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured in an automobile accident. Plaintiff sought to recover for the personal injuries she received from defendant driver's insurer and defendant residence insurer. Plaintiff's father-in-law had an insurance policy with defendant residence insurer. The court held that plaintiff was domiciled at her father-in-law's residence. Thus, defendant residence insurer was liable. The court held that defendant residence insurer was not entitled to a set-off for Medicaid payments under Michigan's No-Fault Insurance Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3109(1), because no benefit existed to be subtracted. Plaintiff also sought recovery for noneconomic losses under § 500.3116. However, as § 500.3116 and § 500.3135 had to be read in conjunction, plaintiff was excluded from recovering noneconomic losses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the findings that: plaintiff was domiciled at her father-in-law's residence; and plaintiff was excluded from recovering noneconomic loss based on statutory construction. The judgment was reversed as to the finding that defendant insurer was entitled to a set-off for governmental Medicaid. Defendant insurer was not so entitled, and this matter was remanded for a disposition consistent with the court's opinion.

O'Donnell v. State Farm Mut. Autombile Ins. Co.


Docket No. 58833


Supreme Court of Michigan


404 Mich. 524; 273 N.W.2d 829; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 422; 10 A.L.R.4th 958


March 3, 1977, Argued  
January 4, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 8, 1979, 406 Mich 1103.
Rehearing denied by O'Donnell v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 406 Mich. 1103, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 1496 (1979)
Appeal dismissed by O'Donnell v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 444 U.S. 803, 100 S. Ct. 22, 62 L. Ed. 2d 16, 1979 U.S. LEXIS 2470 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: 70 Mich App 487; 245 NW2d 801 (1976).

DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed from an order of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) which held that defendant was not entitled to a set-off for federally paid survivor benefits from liabilities owed to plaintiff because the Michigan No-Fault Insurance Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 500.3109, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sought to collect under a personal injury protection provision from defendant insurer. People v. Gallagher


Docket No. 58506


Supreme Court of Michigan


404 Mich. 429; 273 N.W.2d 440; 1979 Mich. LEXIS 419


November 1, 1977, Argued  
January 3, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 68 Mich App 63; 241 NW2d 759 (1976).

 People v Serra, 55 Mich App 514; 223 NW2d 28 (1974), overruled in part.
People v. Gallagher, 68 Mich. App. 63, 241 N.W.2d 759, 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 678 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his appeal from a conviction by a jury of receiving or concealing stolen property and the imposition of a sentence of one to five years imprisonment, which was affirmed by the court of appeals (Michigan), defendant challenged the constitutionality of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.535 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.803) on the grounds that it violated the privilege against self-incrimination, the presumption of innocence, and due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of receiving or concealing stolen property after he was found towing a car lacking a vehicle identification number. Defendant claimed that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.535 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.803) was unconstitutional, but the court disagreed and affirmed the conviction. Under the challenged statute, knowledge that the property was stolen was inferred from evidence that identifying numbers on the property were altered or removed. The court held that evidence that tended to implicate defendant, increasing the pressure on him to testify, did not violate defendant's privilege against self-incrimination. The court also held that the statutory presumption did not violate the presumption of innocence or the requirement of proving defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. There was a rational connection between the proven facts and the fact presumed because using common experience, a dealer who received a car with altered or obliterated identifying numbers likely knew that the car was stolen. Additionally, the jury was properly instructed that the state was required to prove essential elements of the crime, despite the statutory presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for receiving or concealing stolen property.

 

288 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Winford


Docket No. 56983


Supreme Court of Michigan


404 Mich. 400; 273 N.W.2d 54; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 418


April 19, 1977, Argued  
December 29, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 59 Mich App 404; 229 NW2d 474 (1975).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the Michigan Court of Appeals, which reversed defendant's conviction for sexual delinquency and dismissed the charge. The court of appeals held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 767.61a precluded the State, after trial on defendant's principal offense, from filing a supplemental information charging sexual delinquency.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially charged with indecent exposure and convicted. The State filed a supplemental information charging defendant with being a sexually delinquent person, and the jury found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed to the Court of Appeals, which dismissed the sexually delinquent conviction. It ruled that sexual delinquency needed to be charged in the original information charging indecent exposure. On appeal to the Michigan Supreme Court, the court agreed, but for different reasons. The history of sexual delinquency legislation indicated the Legislature's intent to create an alternate sentence for certain specific sexual offenses where evidence appeared to justify a more flexible form of incarceration. The court held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 767.61a did not permit the State to file a sexual delinquency charge after trial to supplement the principal charge. However, it was within the prosecutor's discretion before trial to simultaneously charge the principal offense and the sexual delinquency claim or to proceed solely with the principal offense. After trial on the principal offense began, the State waived the right to charge defendant with sexual delinquency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that reversed defendant's conviction of sexual delinquency and the dismissal of the charge.

People v. Helzer


Docket No. 59064


Supreme Court of Michigan


404 Mich. 410; 273 N.W.2d 44; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 419


January 5, 1978, Argued  
December 29, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 70 Mich App 683; 247 NW2d 328 (1976).
People v. Helzer, 70 Mich. App. 683, 247 N.W.2d 328, 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 902 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed defendant's conviction for gross indecency and sexual delinquency in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.338 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.570) and Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.10a (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.200(1)) and ordered a new trial. The state asserted that the appellate court erred in finding that defendant was entitled to 20 peremptory jury challenges at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for committing two acts of gross indecency with another male, and he was separately convicted by the same jury of being a sexually delinquent person at the time the acts occurred. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the case to the trial court. The court held that defendant was properly given five peremptory jury challenges and convicted of the principal offense of gross indecency. The court held that the trial court erred in allowing the same jury to also decide the matter of sexual delinquency and, further, to deny defendant the right to 20 peremptory jury challenges on that charge. The court found that defendant should be accorded the full 20 peremptory challenges appropriate to the possible life sentence on the sexual delinquency charge. The court stated that the sexual delinquency charge was more than simply a penalty enhancement. The court stated that given the substantial discretion of the jury in hearing the delinquency charge, and the high potential for an automatic conviction when both charges are heard, a separate jury and hearing was required.


OUTCOME: On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction for gross indecency, but reversed the appellate court's order for an entirely new trial. The court remanded for a hearing before a separately empaneled jury on the sexual delinquency charge, and directed the trial court to give defendant 20 peremptory jury challenges.

Higgins v. Monroe Evening News


Docket No. 58842


Supreme Court of Michigan


404 Mich. 1; 272 N.W.2d 537; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 409


November 2, 1977, Argued  
December 26, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 70 Mich App 407; 245 NW2d 769 (1976).
Higgins v. Monroe Evening News, 70 Mich. App. 407, 245 N.W.2d 769, 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 863 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of a decision of the Michigan Court of Appeals, which held that he was not an employee of appellee newspaper for purposes of the workers' compensation laws.


OVERVIEW: The minor was seriously injured when a car struck him while he was helping a friend deliver newspapers. He filed a petition for workers' compensation, but was denied relief because he was not an employee of the newspaper. The Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (board) affirmed that decision, but the court of appeals reversed. On a second hearing, a referee held that the minor was entitled to compensation. The board affirmed, but the court of appeals reversed. The minor appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the minor was not an employee of the newspaper under the workers' compensation laws. The court stated that the workers' compensation laws required the existence of a contract of hire between the minor and the newspaper boy. The court found that the minor had agreed to help deliver newspapers in exchange for "a dime, a pop, or a candy bar." While both parties received a benefit, the court stated that a valid consideration for the contract could not have been presumed from these circumstances. The court found that the evidence illustrated that a social relationship existed between the newsboy and the minor, rather than an employment relationship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that the minor was not an employee of the newspaper for purposes of the workers' compensation laws.

Center Line v. 37th Dist. Court Judges


Docket No. 59520


Supreme Court of Michigan


403 Mich. 595; 271 N.W.2d 526; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 362


March 8, 1978, Argued  
November 20, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 74 Mich App 97; 253 NW2d 669 (1977).
Center Line v. 37th Dist. Court Judges, 74 Mich. App. 97, 253 N.W.2d 669, 1977 Mich. App. LEXIS 703 (1977)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which entered judgment for appellee district judges in the city's action for a declaratory judgment and injunction. The city sought an order that one of the four judges of the judicial district in which the city was located had to sit full time at the city. It alleged that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.9928 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.9928) violated equal protection and due process.


OVERVIEW: The city was located in a third class judicial district. Until 1975, one of the four judges had courtrooms in the city. Another city in the district built a new judicial building, and the city sought to stop the removal of court operations to the new facility. It alleged that all cases had to be heard in the political subdivision in which they arose and that the small claims division had to sit in the city. The circuit court found that only small claims arising in the city and city ordinance violations had to be heard in the city and that remaining court business could be transacted anywhere in the judicial district. The appellate court held further that arraignments on warrants from the city and preliminary examinations on all offenses committed in the city had to be heard in the city. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court and reversed the additional holding of the appellate court. All four judges were to be installed at the new facility because Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.8251(3) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.8251(3)) did not require a full-time judge in the city, only such services of a judge as were consistent with the judicial needs of the district.


OUTCOME: In the city's action to compel the sitting of a full-time judge in the city, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment that small claims and ordinance violations had to be heard in the city but that other court business could be heard anywhere in the district. The court reversed the appellate court's additional holding that arraignments on city warrants and preliminary examinations on all city offenses had to be heard in the city.

Rosario v. Lansing


Docket No. 58025


Supreme Court of Michigan


403 Mich. 124; 268 N.W.2d 230; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 331


June 8, 1977, Argued  
July 24, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 66 Mich App 597; 239 NW2d 428 (1976).
Rosario v. Lansing, 66 Mich. App. 597, 239 N.W.2d 428, 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1226 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a decedent's representative, sought review of an order of the Michigan Court of Appeals that affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendant city in an attractive nuisance action and negligence action against defendants, church and the city.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff represented a child who was found drowned in an open sewer drain in a church parking lot, and filed a lawsuit against the city and a church, alleging negligence, and later amending his complaint to attractive nuisance. The representative contended that defendants knew or should have known that children played in this area, and that the open drain was an attractive nuisance and created an extremely dangerous and hazardous condition for the children playing in the area. The trial court granted the city summary judgment based on governmental immunity, and the court of appeals affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment, holding that the representative had sufficiently pled a claim grounded upon nuisance in fact. Governmental immunity did not bar the claim. Whether or not the open drain was a nuisance was a question for the jury. Therefore, the granting of the summary judgment for the city was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment that was granted in favor of the city.

Shavers v. Attorney General

Writ of certiorari denied Allstate Ins. Co. v. Kelley, 442 U.S. 934, 99 S. Ct. 2869, 61 L. Ed. 2d 303, 1979 U.S. LEXIS 2121 (1979)
Later proceeding at Shavers v. AG, 406 Mich. 1122, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 1550 (1979)
Later proceeding at Shavers v. AG, 407 Mich. 1147, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 448 (1979)
Remanded by Shavers v. AG, 407 Mich. 1153, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 462 (1979)
Decision reached on appeal by Shavers v. AG, 412 Mich. 1105, 315 N.W.2d 130, 1982 Mich. LEXIS 1642 (1982)


PRIOR HISTORY: 65 Mich App 355; 237 NW2d 325 (1975).
Shavers v. Attorney Gen. of Michigan, 65 Mich. App. 355, 237 N.W.2d 325, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 970 (1975)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and reversed in part. Remanded to the trial court for further development of the record.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a ruling of the Michigan Court of Appeals that the Michigan No-Fault Insurance Act 's (Act) personal injury protection scheme and exclusion of two-wheel vehicles were constitutional under the United States and Michigan Constitutions, while the Act's property damage protection scheme was unconstitutional but severable.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought a declaratory judgment regarding the constitutionality of the Michigan No-Fault Insurance Act (Act) under U.S. Const., amend. XIV, Mich. Const. art. 1, § 17. The lower appellate court ruled that the Act's personal injury protection scheme and exclusion of two-wheel vehicles were constitutional, but its property damage protection scheme was unconstitutional and severable. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part, remanding the matter to the trial court for further development of the record. The court granted constitutional approval of the Act's personal injury protection and property damage protection insurance schemata, but held that the Act's compulsory insurance requirement was constitutionally deficient and denied due process by failing to protect motorists from potentially unfair insurance rates, insurance refusal, or insurance cancellation. To permit legislative corrective action, the court ruled that the Act would remain in effect for 18 months from the issuance of its opinion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, finding that the Act's compulsory insurance requirement was constitutionally deficient and denied motorists due process; the court permitted the Act to remain in effect for an additional 18 months to allow legislative correction of deficiencies.

Pultavituma v. H F Campbell Co.


No. 60243


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


402 Mich. 950; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 725



May 23, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Court of Appeals No. 77-1266, order of August 8, 1977.

 

298 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gardner


Docket No. 57633


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


402 Mich. 460; 265 N.W.2d 1; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 392


May 3, 1977, Argued  
April 17, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 65 Mich App 101; 237 NW2d 201 (1975).
People v. Sanford, 65 Mich. App. 101, 237 N.W.2d 201, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 939 (1975)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Court of Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of assault with intent to rob not armed in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.88 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.2830), and were sentenced to 2 to 15 years imprisonment. They sought review, alleging erroneous jury instructions, improper admission of evidence, and violation of their rights with regard to prosecutorial discretion to charge. The Court of Appeals (Michigan) found no reversible error, and the defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the court of appeals, defense counsel alleged a violation of the defendants' right to due process and equal protection because attempted robbery unarmed was an identical offense to the one with which the defendants were charged and carried only a five-year sentence. On review, the court held that assault with intent to rob not armed, and attempted robbery unarmed, were not identical crimes. Assault with intent to rob not armed required the use of force and violence. Attempted robbery unarmed may be committed without force and violence simply by putting another in fear. Sufficient evidence in the record established that the defendants received a fair trial, even though the trial judge gave no instruction on the requirement of a unanimous verdict. The jury instruction on witness identification testimony was substantially similar to that requested and there was no prejudice. The complaining witness's testimony about calling police and identifying the defendants in a pool hall was not hearsay and was properly admitted. The testimony of the police officer, who testified only to the circumstances of the identification, was properly admitted within the trial judge's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals upholding defendants' convictions.

Westervelt v. Natural Resources Com.


Docket No. 57349


Supreme Court of Michigan


402 Mich. 412; 263 N.W.2d 564; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 391


June 10, 1976, Argued  
March 20, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 62 Mich App 539; 233 NW2d 640 (1975).
Westervelt v. Natural Resources Com., 62 Mich. App. 539, 233 N.W.2d 640, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1087 (1975)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed and the case is remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, boat and canoe livery operators, sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the trial court's denial of their motion for a declaratory judgment against defendants, the Department of Natural Resources (department) and its director, to ascertain whether certain rules promulgated by the department were invalid.


OVERVIEW: The department passed rules, which were designed to regulate certain state rivers. The rules applied only to those persons who had or rented watercraft in a stretch of a river designated for non-motor watercraft use. The operators sought a declaratory judgment as to the validity of the proposed rules, contending that they were unconstitutional and an invalid delegation of legislative power. The department contended that the court of appeals erred in holding that the rules were void and were promulgated pursuant to a statute which impermissibly delegated rule-making power to the department. The court held that: (1) Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 299.3, 299.3a (Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 13.3, 13.4) satisfied the constitutional principle of the separation of powers in providing standards as reasonably precise as the subject matter of the legislation required, plus the safeguards inherent in the statutes provided constitutionally sufficient protection to the people as required by due process and (2) the evidence was insufficient to determine whether the delegation of rule-making power to the department pursuant to the statutes was a constitutionally valid delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals, which found the river rules to be unconstitutional, was reversed, and the case was remanded to determine the issue of whether the rivers rules exceeded the scope of authority delegated.

 

300 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Forest v. Parmalee


Docket Nos. 56973, 56974, 56794, 58647


Supreme Court of Michigan


402 Mich. 348; 262 N.W.2d 653; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 384


June 7, 1977, Argued  
February 27, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 60 Mich App 401; 231 NW2d 378 (1975).
Forest v. Parmalee, 60 Mich. App. 401, 231 N.W.2d 378, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 654 (1975)



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the Court of Appeals are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, three injured parties, brought separate actions against defendants, three governmental tortfeasors, for injuries sustained from the governmental tortfeasors negligence. The claims were dismissed based on the two-year statute of limitations contained in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1411 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(111)). The Court of Appeals (Michigan) affirmed the dismissals. The cases were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The injured parties alleged the two-year statute of limitations applicable to claims brought against governmental tortfeasors for injuries resulting from negligently maintained highways was violative of equal protection because the comparable statute of limitations applicable to the same claims brought against private tortfeasors was three years. The court upheld the dismissals, finding that the time limit was neither arbitrary nor capricious and did not violate equal protection. State legislatures had a broad range of discretion in establishing classifications in the exercise of their police powers, and if a reasonable relationship existed between the governmental classification and a legitimate state interest, no denial of equal protection resulted. The injured parties presented no cogent showing that the statute of limitations had operated arbitrarily or capriciously in barring their causes of action and there was a rational basis for enacting a shorter statute of limitations for victims of governmental tortfeasors than for victims of private tortfeasors. The legislature could place reasonable restrictions on the right to bring a claim against governmental tortfeasors.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals that the statute of limitations did not violate equal protection was affirmed.

Greenfield Constr. Co. v. Dep't of State Hwys


Docket No. 56686


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


402 Mich. 172; 261 N.W.2d 718; 1978 Mich. LEXIS 370


June 8, 1976, Argued  
January 25, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 17, 1978, post, p 962.
Rehearing denied by Greenfield Constr. Co. v. Dep't of State Hwys, 402 Mich. 961, 1978 Mich. LEXIS 1034 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: 58 Mich App 49; 227 NW2d 223 (1975).
Greenfield Constr. Co. v. Michigan Dep't of State Highways, 58 Mich. App. 49, 227 N.W.2d 223, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1666 (1975)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed by an equally divided Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff construction company sought review of a judgment from the lower appellate court (Michigan) ruling that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to have adjudicated plaintiff's claim against defendant state department of highways. Plaintiff filed a claim seeking extra compensation and an extension of the construction period.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff construction company contracted with defendant highway department to construct sewer outlet structures into a lake. Plaintiff alleged a change in the conditions of the work site due to an increase in the water level by two feet; plaintiff requested and was denied excess compensation in a letter by defendant. The lower appellate court ruled that the circuit court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the lower appellate court. The court held the 1970 Standard Specifications for Highway Construction which were the basis of rejection as stated in defendant's letter were not rules within the definition of the Administrative Procedure Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 24.263; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.560(163) and the court therefore held the specifications were not reviewable. The court further held that under common law the trial court did not have jurisdiction to have issued a declaratory judgment. The court therefore ruled that the trial court had lacked subject matter jurisdiction to have issued a ruling stating plaintiff was entitled to extra compensation due to changed physical conditions and an extension of time for construction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower appellate court on the grounds that defendant state highway department's letter that invoked highway construction rules was not reviewable under statutory law and therefore the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to have granted relief to plaintiff construction company.

McAvoy v. H. B. Sherman Co.


Docket Nos. 58845, 58846, 58983, 58855


Supreme Court of Michigan


401 Mich. 419; 258 N.W.2d 414; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 116


February 1, 1977, Argued  
October 11, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied and motion for clarification granted 402 Mich 953.
Rehearing denied by McAvoy v. H B Sherman Co., 402 Mich. 953, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1505 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Turner v. General Motors Corp., Fisher Body Plant, 70 Mich. App. 532, 246 N.W.2d 631, 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 879 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employers and insurers, challenged the decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which dismissed their appeals from decisions of hearing referees for failure to comply with Mich. Comp. Laws § 418.862. Appellants challenged the constitutionality of that statute and the Appeal Board's authority to enforce the statute by dismissing their appeals.


OVERVIEW: Appellee former employees received workers' compensation benefits. Appellants, employers and insurers, sought review before the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (board). After the enactment of Mich. Comp. Laws § 418.862, the board ordered payment of 70 percent of the benefits awarded during the pendency of the appeals. Appellants refused to pay until the constitutional challenge to § 418.862 was resolved. The board dismissed appellants' challenges for failure to comply with the payment order. The court of appeals affirmed. Appellants challenged the judgment, seeking a declaration that the amendment was unconstitutional and injunctive relief to prevent enforcement of § 418.862. The court affirmed, holding, inter alia, that the guarantee of due process demanded only that the law was not to be unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious, and that the means selected were to have a real and substantial relation to the object sought to be attained. Due process did not necessarily guarantee appellants a right to a complete stay of benefits while the awards were reviewed.


OUTCOME: The judgment ordering appellants, employers and insurers, to pay benefits awarded during the pendency of the challenge was affirmed. Due process demanded only that the law was not to be unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious, and that the means selected were to have a substantial relation to the object sought to be attained. Due process did not guarantee appellants a right to a complete stay of benefits while an award was reviewed.

Cramer v. Metropolitan Sav. & Loan Asso.


Docket No. 57215


Supreme Court of Michigan


401 Mich. 252; 258 N.W.2d 20; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 103


October 7, 1976, Argued  
October 6, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 402 Mich 954, 960.
Rehearing denied by, Motion denied by Cramer v. Metro. S&L Ass'n, 402 Mich. 954, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1515 (1977)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cramer v. Metropolitan Federal Sav. & Loan Asso., 436 U.S. 958, 98 S. Ct. 3072, 57 L. Ed. 2d 1123, 1978 U.S. LEXIS 2199 (1978)
Rehearing denied by, Stay denied by, As moot Cramer v. Metro. S&L Ass'n, 402 Mich. 959, 1978 Mich. LEXIS 1081 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cramer v. Metropolitan Federal Sav. & Loan Asso., 34 Mich. App. 638, 192 N.W.2d 50, 1971 Mich. App. LEXIS 1658 (1971)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff mortgagor sought relief from foreclosure on property by the defendant savings and loan after the latter accelerated the debt. A verdict was entered for the savings and loan on a breach of fiduciary duty count brought by the mortgagor. After the third appeal, a Michigan court of appeals affirmed the verdict. The Supreme Court of Michigan granted leave to consider allegations of error in all of the proceedings below.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagor executed a mortgage application to the savings and loan. There was a continuing dispute, however, over the escrow account, and the mortgagor alleged that the savings and loan had not paid her taxes and escrow premiums when due and that it was requiring excessive escrow payments. The savings and loan admitted that it allowed the taxes to become delinquent, but paid the back taxes, including all penalties. The savings and loan foreclosed after the mortgagor finally stopped the escrow payments, and stated that she wished to make her tax and insurance payments directly. The mortgagor questioned the constitutionality of the foreclosure by advertisement statute and argued that the mortgage provisions constituted a covenant, the remedy for breach of which was an action for damages or an injunction. The savings and loan contended that the monthly payments into escrow were a condition, and default thereon allowed foreclosure by advertisement. The court held the claim of unconstitutionality failed for lack of the existence of state action and that foreclosure was permissible because the mortgagor failed to perform a covenant the performance of which was a contract condition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial and appellate courts' judgment that the mortgagor had defaulted on the mortgage and that foreclosure was appropriate.

 

307 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Crawl


Docket No. 56294


Supreme Court of Michigan


401 Mich. 1; 257 N.W.2d 86; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 154


January 5, 1977, Argued  
August 29, 1977, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), convicting him of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in admitting evidence seized during an impermissible search and seizure. The court ruled that an arrest in a residence did not justify a general search of the residence, and that there was no justification for routinely searching any room other than that in which an arrest occurred. Further, the court held that while warrantless protective searches could be justified when reasonably necessary to prevent the dangers that a suspect at large in the house could resist or escape, once all persons occupying the residence were under supervision and control and there was no reason to believe that anyone else was present, the rationale for a protective search no longer obtained and a further search could not be conducted. The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that although a warrantless search could be conducted incident to a lawful arrest, an arrest made outside the arrestee's residence did not justify a subsequent search of the residence.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was reversed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judicial tenure commission asked the court to accept its recommendation that respondent judge be removed from judicial office and permanently enjoined from holding any judicial office in the future following its findings of numerous acts of judicial misconduct.

OUTCOME: Recommendation asking that the judge be removed from judicial office and permanently enjoined from holding any judicial office was denied, and the court ordered that the judge be suspended from office for a period of five years without salary.

Ford Motor Co. v. Michigan State Tax Com.


Docket No. 57787


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 499; 255 N.W.2d 608; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 147


February 2, 1977, Argued  
July 18, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Ford Motor Co. v. State Tax Comm'n, 401 Mich. 952, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1242 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ford Motor Co. v. Michigan State Tax Com., 63 Mich. App. 577, 234 N.W.2d 711, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1202 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Michigan State Tax Commission, city, and school district, appealed a judgment by the Michigan Court of Appeals, which held that plaintiff taxpayer could elect under Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.13 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 7.13) to be assessed on tax day in one assessing district and elect to be assessed on the average monthly inventory in another.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, who owned inventories in more than one assessing district within the same county, elected to be assessed on tax day in one assessing district and elected to be assessed on the average monthly inventory in another. The city determined that he could not make contrary elections under Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.13 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 7.13) within the same county, and the tax commission agreed. The court of appeals disagreed, holding that the taxpayer could make different elections in different assessing districts. The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals. The court held that the statute was plain and unequivocal on its face. The statute in plain words referred solely to assessing districts. Therefore, the statute gave the taxpayer an election, which it could exercise in each assessing district of the state in which it had inventories independent of elections it made in other assessing districts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals that the taxpayer could elect to be assessed on tax day in one assessing district and elect to be assessed on the average monthly inventory in another.

Avis Rent-A-Car System, Inc. v. Romulus Community Schools


Docket Nos. 57857, 57936, 57937


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 337; 254 N.W.2d 555; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 141


April 19, 1977, Argued  
June 13, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 401 Mich 951.
Rehearing denied by Avis Rent-A-Car Sys. v. City of Romulus, 401 Mich. 951, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1238 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Avis Rent-A-Car System, Inc. v. Romulus, 65 Mich. App. 119, 237 N.W.2d 209, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 941 (1975)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city and school district, sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the grant of appellee taxpayers' motion for summary judgment in an action to determine the constitutionality of 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts 174, under which taxes were imposed on the taxpayers.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers held concessions to operate automobile leasing facilities at the county airport. Appellants' attempt to assess taxes against the taxpayers was rebuffed under 1953 Mich. Pub. Acts 189, which granted such concessionaires a tax exemption. The act was subsequently amended by 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts 174, which stated that the exemption did not apply to airport concessionaires in counties having a population in excess of one million people. Appellants again attempted to assess taxes against the taxpayers. The taxpayers brought separate actions challenging the act as unconstitutional under Mich. Const. art. 4, § 29. Both taxpayers sought, and were granted, summary judgment. Appellants sought review and the court affirmed. The court noted that art. 4, § 29 prohibited the passing of any local or special act where a general act could have been made applicable. Because Wayne County, where appellants were located, was the only county in Michigan that met the population requirement of 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts 174, the court found that the act was a local act. The court further found no reasonable relationship between withdrawing the taxpayers' exemption and the size of the county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision that held unconstitutional an act that denied the taxpayers an exemption from appellants' taxing authority.

In re Advisory Opinion Re Constitutionality of P.A. 1975 No. 301


Docket No. 57918


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 270; 254 N.W.2d 528; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 193


June 8, 1976, Submitted  
June 10, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Request for Advisory Opinion on 1975 Pa 301, 396 Mich. 951, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 594 (1976)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Statute declared constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court was requested to advise whether the Derezinski-Geerlings Job Development Authority Act, Mich. Con. Laws Ann. § 125.1702, complied with various provisions of the Michigan Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The Derezinski-Geerlings Job Development Authority Act, (Act) Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 125.1702, was enacted to create a job development authority and to alleviate and prevent unemployment. The authority would have had the power to make loans to finance projects with uncertain prospects and revenue projections. The projects anticipated included pollution control and energy development projects. The authority could issue bonds but did not have the power to bind the taxing authority of the state and bondholders could not force the state to cover a deficiency in case of a default. The court found the Act constitutional and held that the Act provided for public internal improvements, which was an exception to Mich. Const. art 3, § 6 that prohibited state involvement in internal improvements. The court also held that the appropriation of funds would be for a public purpose as required by Mich. Const. art 4, § 30 and not a private purpose. Finally, the court held that the Act complied with Mich. Const. art. 9 §§ 12, 15, & 18 because the public authority established by the Act could only administer self-liquidating projects that did not create a debt obligation for the state.


OUTCOME: The court found that the Derezinski-Geerlings Job Development Authority Act complied with the Michigan Constitution.

 

312 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stanton


Docket No. 58626


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 192; 253 N.W.2d 650; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 136



June 2, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On application by the defendant for leave to appeal the Supreme Court, in lieu of granting leave to appeal, reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Michigan Court of Appeals, which reversed the trial court's decision to quash the information that charged defendant with being an inmate in possession of a weapon that could have been used to injure a convict or to assist a convict to escape pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 800.283, 1909 Mich. Pub. Acts 17, as amended by 1972 Mich. Pub. Acts 105.


OVERVIEW: The determinative issue was whether the 1972 amendment to § 3 of 1909 Mich. Pub. Acts 17 violated the title-object limitation in Mich. Const. art. 4, § 24 (1963). The Act was designed to keep weapons, liquor, and narcotics out of the state prison system. It was aimed at persons bringing those items into a prison. In reversing the appellate court's decision, the court found that the 1972 amendment enlarged the scope of the person subject to prosecution under the Act to include the convicts themselves should they control or have possession of a prescribed weapon. The body of the statute, as amended, spoke more broadly that its restrictively-speaking title. The title failed to reveal the existence of the new criminal class created by the amendment. The omission in the title was fatal and rendered the 1972 amendment unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court.

In re Request for Advisory Opinion Enrolled Senate Bill


Docket No. 58691


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 311; 254 N.W.2d 544; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 194

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Act declared constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court was the Michigan Legislature's request for an advisory opinion on whether 1964 Mich. Pub. Acts 183 (the act), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 830.411 et seq., (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.447(101) et seq.), violated Mich. Const. art. 9, §§ 12 and 15.


OVERVIEW: The Michigan Legislature enacted the act, which provided for the state to lease property from the State Building Authority and for the payment of rent on the leased premises at fixed times over a period of years. The legislature requested an advisory opinion from the court regarding the constitutionality of the act. Specifically, the legislature requested an opinion as to whether the act violated the provisions of the constitution that placed limitations on the power of the legislature to borrow money and issue evidence of the debt thereby incurred. The court concluded that the obligation to pay rent under a lease did not involve borrowing. Consequently it did not result in the incurring of a debt as that word was used in the limitations set forth. Therefore, the court held that the act was constitutional, and the legislature was authorized to enter into lease agreements, and pay rent thereunder.


OUTCOME: The act that authorized the lease of property and the payment of rent thereunder was declared constitutional.

 

315 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Stanton v. Lloyd Hammond Produce Farms


Docket No. 58154


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 135; 253 N.W.2d 114; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 131


February 2, 1977, Argued  
May 6, 1977, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed a decision of the appeals board and affirmed the referee's award to plaintiff employee of medical expenses and weekly wage benefits, under the Michigan Worker's Disability Compensation Act of 1969, Mich. Comp. Laws § 418.115(d) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.237(115)(d)).


OVERVIEW: The employee was an agricultural worker. Upon returning to work from a delivery, the employee was injured in an accident. Before returning to work, he stopped at his sister's home to request a ride home. This detour took him approximately 10 miles out of his way. The accident occurred soon after leaving his sister's home. The workers' compensation referee awarded him medical expenses and weekly benefits. The appeals board reversed the award of weekly wages. The appeals court affirmed the referee, and on review, the court affirmed the findings of the appeals court. The court retroactively applied a case decided after the employee's accident, which held that an agricultural exclusion in the Act was unconstitutional. The court held that it was a general rule of statutory interpretation that an unconstitutional statute was void ab initio. The court held that the employee's injuries arose out of the course of his employment, as the detour to his sister's home was only a slight deviation, and therefore, compensable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the findings of the appeals court. The court held that the appeals court did not err in affirming the findings of the referee, which awarded the employee medical expenses and weekly wage benefits.

 

316 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Frost-Pack Distributing Co. v. Grand Rapids


Docket No. 55930


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 664; 252 N.W.2d 747; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 177


March 6, 1975, Argued  
May 2, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Frost--Pack Distributing Co. v. Grand Rapids, 52 Mich. App. 694, 218 N.W.2d 75, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1089 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) that affirmed a judgment of the trial court entered in favor of defendant city in an action for a refund of personal property taxes. The taxpayer contended that farm products stored in a public warehouse owned by a subsidiary of the taxpayer were exempt from taxation pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.9 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 7.9).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer paid personal property taxes under protest and filed an action for a refund of the taxes. The trial court and the court of appeals held that the property at issue was not exempt from taxation. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the taxpayer, who was storing farm products in a public warehouse that were not in transit to out of state destinations, could claim an exemption under Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.9 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 7.9) because he was not a consignor within the meaning of the statute. Section 211.9 denied personal property tax exemptions to consignors who stored property in a warehouse operated by a subsidiary. The court held that pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.9 para. 14th (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 7.9 para. 14th) farm products stored in a public warehouse were exempt from taxation whether or not they were destined for use inside or outside the state, or whether their destination was unascertained at the time.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals entered in favor of the city in the taxpayer's action for a tax refund and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

317 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Stottlemeyer v. General Motors Corp.


Docket No. 56626


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 605; 250 N.W.2d 486; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 170


February 4, 1976, Argued  
February 14, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Stottlemeyer v. GMC, 394 Mich. 814, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 568 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employers challenged a decision of the Michigan Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board, which affirmed a referee's decision that the employers were not entitled to reimbursement from appellee Silicosis and Dust Disease Fund for compensation paid to a worker for his disability caused by emphysema and fibrosis because those diseases were not "other dust diseases" as defined in Mich. Comp. Laws § 417.5 and were thus not compensable.


OVERVIEW: The liability for the worker's benefits was apportioned among his employers, who sought reimbursement from the Fund for all benefits paid to him in excess of $ 12,500 claiming that the "other dust diseases" clause of Mich. Comp. Laws § 417.5 included the worker's pulmonary emphysema and fibrosis with chronic bronchitis caused by exposure to dust, fumes, and other irritants, as found by the referee. On review, the court found that the legislative history of § 417.5 indicated that its purpose was to protect industries and employers from undue financial burden by establishing a reimbursement scheme through the Fund. The court held that "other dust disease" was limited to silicosis, pneumoconiosis, or other dust diseases posing a threat to an industry comparable to the mining, quarrying, and grinding industries, and that the burden of proving that a disease was so common as to pose such a threat remained with an employer. The court ruled that § 417.5's scheme of taxing all businesses for the benefit of a few industries was not a violation of due process or equal protection where the State had a rational purpose in protecting industries from statutory compensation requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.

 

318 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tyler


Docket Nos. 55396, 55397


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 564; 250 N.W.2d 467; 1977 Mich. LEXIS 167


September 13, 1974, Argued  
February 14, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Michigan v. Tyler, 436 U.S. 499, 98 S. Ct. 1942, 56 L. Ed. 2d 486, 1978 U.S. LEXIS 97 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Tyler, 50 Mich. App. 414, 213 N.W.2d 221, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 926 (1973)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of conspiracy to burn real property, and one defendant was convicted of burning real property and burning insured property with the intent to defraud. At trial, defendants objected to evidence obtained at the fire scene without a search warrant. The Court of Appeals (Michigan) affirmed the trial court's ruling admitting the evidence over objection. Defendants appealed the ruling and their convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that their convictions were obtained through the improper admission of evidence collected at the fire scene by fire fighters acting without a search warrant. The court overturned defendants' convictions and ordered a new trial. In so holding, the court found that 1) probable cause and a warrant were required to enter into private property, even if the investigation at the fire scene is to determine the cause of the fire; 2) at the point where the fire investigator focused his attention on assembling proof of arson, a criminal investigation began and a warrant was required to enter into defendant's property; 3) evidence acquired while the firefighters were lawfully on the property was admissible under the plain view doctrine; 4) exigent circumstances did not justify the fire investigator's warrantless search made weeks after the fire was extinguished; 5) defendant continued to have a reasonable expectation of privacy in his property even after it had been burned.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Fourth Amendment's prohibition against warrantless searches was applicable to property damaged by fire. The court reversed the trial court's ruling and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

319 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pummer


Docket No. 57200


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 326; 249 N.W.2d 78; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 219


April 5, 1976, Argued  
December 31, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Pummer, 61 Mich. App. 552, 233 N.W.2d 79, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1564 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded to the Court of Appeals for a decision on the substantive issues.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which dismissed the State's appeal from the trial court's decision to grant defendant a new trial on his charge of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder but before he could be sentenced the trial court granted defendant's motion for new trial. The appellate court granted the State's application for leave to appeal the order granting new trial but later dismissed the appeal on the grounds that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 770.12 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.1109) did not authorize the State to appeal an order granting new trial. The court reversed the decision of the appellate court and found that and found that appeals by the State were governed by Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.308 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.308) and the rules of the court. Final judgments were appealable as of right under Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 806.1 (1963) and interlocutory orders were appealable by leave under Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 806.2 (1963). Because an order for new trial led to further proceedings and did not cut off any acquired rights, it was a nonfinal, interlocutory order. The State proceeded correctly in applying for leave to appeal to the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision to dismiss the State's appeal from the trial court's order granting defendant a new trial and remand the cause for a decision on the substantive issues raised by the State.

State Bar v. Cramer


Docket No. 56413


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 116; 249 N.W.2d 1; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 210


November 6, 1975, Argued  
December 30, 1976, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan) entered an order permanently enjoining defendant businesswoman from holding herself out to be qualified to render advice and service regarding divorce, rendering counsel and service to persons seeking divorce, and furnishing divorce kits with assistance in their completion. The businesswoman was also found to be in contempt of the injunction on more than one occasion.


OVERVIEW: The businesswoman sold divorce kits, assisted in completing the kits, and gave advice about obtaining a divorce to her customers. Plaintiff state bar alleged that the businesswoman's conducted constituted the unauthorized practice of law, in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws M 600.916, Mich. Stat. Ann. 27A.916. The first time she violated the order her punishment was conditional upon her promise to stop the business. The following times she had to stay in jail. Upon review, the court determined that all but her first sentence were punishment for behavior already committed in violation of the decree and that the contempt action, being unconditional as to result was criminal and improper. The court concluded that because the business woman offered counsel in the form of professional guidance to persons seeking to extricate themselves from a legal relationship, the party represented and the public in general, had a right to be assured that their interests were properly represented by members of the bar. The court held that to the extent that the businesswoman provided personal advice peculiar to the dissolution of a specific marriage, she was engaged in the unauthorized practice of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the injunctive order entered by the trial court and the finding of civil contempt when the businesswoman was first convicted but reversed and vacated the remainder of the contempt convictions because they were criminal in nature.

Northview Constr. Co. v. St. Clair Shores


Docket No. 54712


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 184; 249 N.W.2d 290; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 212


January 27, 1976, Submitted on Rehearing  
December 30, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 400 Mich 952.
Rehearing denied by Northview Constr. Co. v. City of St Clair Shores (On Rehearing), 400 Mich. 952, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 683 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Argued March 14, 1974 (Calendar No. 10). Decided December 18, 1975, 395 Mich 497. Rehearing granted 395 Mich 924.
Northview Constr. Co. v. St. Clair Shores, 395 Mich. 497, 236 N.W.2d 396, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 180 (1975)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed by an equally divided Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class representatives sought a rehearing of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which dismissed the class action because the class representatives did not adequately represent the class after they secured judgment against defendant homeowners in their favor alone.


OVERVIEW: The class representatives filed a class action pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 208.1(3) (1963). The class representatives were contractors who sought payment for services rendered to homeowners. After 15 years of litigation, the trial court granted them a summary judgment on their claims alone, prior to the appearance of any other member of the class. The trial court ordered notice by publication to other potential class members and then dismissed the class action. The court of appeals refused to rule on the form of notice because there was not adequate representation to justify continuation of the class action. The court agreed with the court of appeals that a class action could continue, when the named complainant's claim was moot, where a statute or procedure was challenged on grounds of constitutionality or misapplication. In the instant case, in contrast, the class representatives sought collection of money, which was not an unconstitutional practice. The class representatives were happy with their satisfied judgments. They were no longer capable of properly representing the class because they no longer shared common issues and interests with unpaid class members.


OUTCOME: On rehearing, the court affirmed the court of appeals' decision to dismiss the class action because the class representatives secured judgment in their favor alone prior to the intervention of any other member of the class.

American Federation of State, County & Municipal Employees v. Recorder's Court Judges


Docket No. 57235


Supreme Court of Michigan


399 Mich. 1; 248 N.W.2d 220; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 205; 94 L.R.R.M. 2392


March 4, 1976, Argued  
December 27, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 400 Mich 952.
Rehearing denied by Council No 23, Local 1905 v. Recorder's Court Judges, 400 Mich. 952, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 701 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Council No 23, Local 1905 v. Recorder's Court Judges, 395 Mich. 804, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 731 (1975)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant probation officer challenged the refusal of appellee Recorder's Court Judges (Michigan), to enter into binding arbitration on the grievance that the officer filed concerning his discharge from employment pursuant to the provisions of Mich. Comp. Laws § 771.10; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.1140.


OVERVIEW: The Recorder's Court Judges, after notice and hearing, found officer incompetent or guilty of misconduct, neglect of duty, or refusal to carry out the order of the court and recommended to the state Corrections Commission his removal pursuant to the probation officer removal statute. Appellant union filed a grievance requesting arbitration pursuant to the statute, but the Recorder's Court declined to submit. The union unsuccessfully sought mandamus in the court of appeals. The union and officer appealed. The court believed that the specific provision of § 771.10 should have been held to be the only procedure necessary for the discharge of a probation officer. It guaranteed the officer a full hearing at which the court had to determine incompetence or misconduct before it could recommend removal. The court held that there was no repeal of the probation officer removal statute with the Public Employees Relations Act § 423.201 et seq., as there was no specific legislative language, and repeal by implication was not favored. Therefore, the court held the two statutes had to be construed together and that no review by binding arbitration of the decision to remove the officer was needed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

323 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People of Adrian v. Poucher


Docket No. 58074


Supreme Court of Michigan


398 Mich. 316; 247 N.W.2d 798; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 185



December 21, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] On application by the defendant for leave to appeal the Supreme Court, in lieu of granting leave to appeal, affirmed the decision of the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Michigan) upheld the constitutionality of an ordinance which required a motorcyclist to wear a crash helmet, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In an earlier, unrelated matter, the appellate court determined that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.658(d), which required motorcyclists to wear helmets, was unconstitutional. However, when defendant's case was before the appellate court for review, the appellate court upheld ordinance language identical to the statute. Defendant sought review of the determination, arguing that the interests of the public did not require interference with his right to drive a motorcycle without a helmet. The court held that a requirement that a helmet be worn provided protection, not only to the motorcyclist, but the other drivers who could be involved in an accident with the motorcyclist. Due to the statistical information that indicated the added safety of wearing a helmet, and the minor burden such a requirement imposed on motorcyclists, the court found that the legislature was entitled to require that helmets be worn. The court determined that the legislature had the power to control and regulate the use of the highways and the regulation served a public interest.


OUTCOME: In lieu of granting defendant leave to appeal the appellate court's decision, the court affirmed the finding that an ordinance requiring motorcyclists to wear crash helmets was constitutional.

Hobbs v. Michigan State Highway Dep't


Docket No. 56990


Supreme Court of Michigan


398 Mich. 90; 247 N.W.2d 754; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 171


May 5, 1976, Argued  
December 7, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Hobbs v. Michigan State Highway Dep't, 58 Mich. App. 189, 227 N.W.2d 286, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1687 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed and remanded to the Court of Claims for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state highway department (state) appealed from a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) reversing the summary judgment granted in the state's favor on the grounds that plaintiff estate's action was time-barred pursuant to the Court of Claims Act (Act), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.6431(1) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.6431(1)).


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed May 22, 1972, when his car plunged off an overpass bridge onto a state highway. Suit was filed against the state on October 9, 1973 alleging negligent bridge design and construction. The lower court granted summary judgment to the state, finding the claim was time-barred. The court of appeals reversed, holding that the two-year statute of limitations in the governmental liability act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1411(2) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(111)(2)), governed the case. The court affirmed, as the negligence claim arose under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1402 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(102)), which imposed liability on the state for damages caused by breach of its statutory duty to maintain highways in safe condition. The court next addressed whether the claim was barred for failure to give notice to the state within 120 days after the cause of action accrued, under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1404 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(104)). It held that the notice requirement did not apply because the state failed to show prejudice for the estate's failure to timely notify it of its intent to file a claim. The court affirmed and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals granting summary judgment to the state against the estate in the estate's action for negligent bridge design, and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Cruz v. Chevrolet Grey Iron, Div. of General Motors Corp.


Docket No. 56032


Supreme Court of Michigan


398 Mich. 117; 247 N.W.2d 764; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 174


May 8, 1975, Argued  
December 7, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 399 Mich 1041.
Rehearing denied by Cruz v. Chevrolet Grey Iron Div. of GMC, 399 Mich. 1041, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1497 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cruz v. Chevrolet Grey Iron, Div. of General Motors Corp., 53 Mich. App. 472, 220 N.W.2d 178, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1159 (1974)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sought review of a decision by the Michigan Court of Appeals, which found that the application of the Workmen's Compensation Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.357 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.237(357)), providing for reduction in compensation payments to the claimant as an employee over the age of 65, was constitutional and did not deny him equal protection of the law.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured while at work. In computing the benefit, the workmen's compensation appeals board applied Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.357 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.237(357)), which provided for reduction in compensation payments to the claimant as an employee over the age of 65. The lower court affirmed this application. Upon appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the plain meaning of the words and the logical interpretation of the statute led to the conclusion that its provisions fell equally upon all regardless of age at the time of injury. The court found that the legislature recognized diminishing earning capacity in the diminishing life expectancy of the older worker and developed a 5 percent reduction formula for each year after the 65th birthday. The court held that while the formula may not have precisely reflected the loss of anticipated earnings of each individual, the statute was comprehensive and constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the application of a the Workmen's Compensation Act, which provided for a reduction of the claimant's workmen's compensation benefits based on his age, as constitutional.
