328 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Pittman v. Taylor


Docket No. 54854


Supreme Court of Michigan


398 Mich. 41; 247 N.W.2d 512; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 169


May 9, 1974, Argued; April 7, 1976, Reargued  
November 23, 1976, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff student appealed an order from the trial court (Michigan), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant city in the student's personal injury action against the city and defendants, the Board of Education, individual teachers, and a chemical manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The student, a 16-year old, was provided with chemicals by school teachers to construct a rocket as a science project. The student mixed the chemicals at his home, an explosion resulted, and he was severely injured. The student sued the city, the board, and the teachers. The city successfully sought summary judgment, arguing that the town's Board of Education was an agency of the state over which the city had no control, thus, the city could not be liable for the board's actions. On appeal, the court vacated and remanded the order, finding that because the claim arose prior to the enactment of 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts 155, which cured the constitutional defect found in the voided 1964 Governmental Immunity Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1407, the claim was subject to common-law governmental tort immunity. The court then found that the doctrine of sovereign immunity was an exception to the fundamental concept of tort law that liability followed tortious conduct, that individuals and corporations were responsible for their actions, and that traditional common-law judge-made immunity that the state and its instrumentalities theretofore had enjoyed from its torts was abrogated.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order granting the city summary judgment in the student's personal injury action, held that the common-law doctrine of state governmental immunity was abrogated, and remanded the case for further proceedings. The ruling was to be prospective, with the exception of the instant case and any pending cases in which an express challenge to the common-law defense of state governmental immunity had been made and preserved.

People v. Mauch


Docket No. 56756


Supreme Court of Michigan


397 Mich. 646; 247 N.W.2d 5; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 323


March 4, 1976, Argued  
November 23, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Filed January 10, 1977.
Rehearing denied by People v. Mauch, 400 Mich. 951, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 645 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Mauch, 394 Mich. 825, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 597 (1975)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which set- aside defendant's guilty plea to kidnapping charges.


OVERVIEW: While serving a life sentence on non-related charges, defendant entered a guilty plea to kidnapping charges. Defendant alleged that the trial court failed to acknowledge his guilt as to every element of the offense. The appellate court set the guilty plea aside, on appeal, the court reversed the appellate court and reinstated the guilty plea. The court held that because defendant's plea was entered prior to the enactment of the more stringent plea requirements, the trial court was not required to obtain defendant's acknowledgement of his guilt as to each and every element of the crime of kidnapping. The court further held that under the standard by which defendant's plea was judged, the trial court sufficiently inquired into the voluntariness of defendant's plea. The court also held that the trial court sufficiently advised defendant of the consequences of his plea as was required pursuant to Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 35A (1945). Finally, the court held that the trial court's failure to prepare a presentence report did not require that defendant be remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the appellate court, which set-aside defendant's guilty plea to kidnapping charges.

McNitt v. Citco Drilling Co.


Docket Nos. 56871, 57375


Supreme Court of Michigan


397 Mich. 384; 245 N.W.2d 18; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 306


March 3, 1976, Argued  
August 26, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: McNitt v. Citco Drilling Co., 60 Mich. App. 81, 230 N.W.2d 318, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1420 (1975)
Gilbert v. Leach, 62 Mich. App. 722, 233 N.W.2d 840, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1116 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The cases are remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Michigan) held in two consolidated appeals that the results of tests administered pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.625a (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 9.2325(1) could not be used in civil litigation in wrongful death lawsuits. Plaintiff administrator of the estate of a drunken driver (administrator) in the first case and defendant driver both had sought to exclude the evidence of blood alcohol.


OVERVIEW: In two appeals, the common issue concerned the admissibility of the result of a blood alcohol test in civil litigation. In the first action for wrongful death, the administrator sought to exclude the evidence. In the second cause of action, the driver sought to exclude the evidence. The court of appeals ruled that the test results could not be used in civil litigation in wrongful death lawsuits, such as those before it. On appeal, the court affirmed the holding that the results of tests administered pursuant to statutory mandate could not be used in civil litigation. The legislature had limited the authority of police officers to request hospital personnel to withdraw blood or otherwise test for blood alcohol content without consent and had limited the use that may be made of blood alcohol test results obtained pursuant to exercise of that authority. The trial court properly excluded the evidence because of the invalidity of any alleged consent.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals in two consolidated appeals, which held that the results of blood alcohol tests could not be used in civil litigation in wrongful death lawsuits pursuant to the administrator's and the driver's motions to exclude, was affirmed.

Michigan Canners & Freezers Asso. v. Agricultural Marketing & Bargaining Bd.


Docket No. 56434


Supreme Court of Michigan


397 Mich. 337; 245 N.W.2d 1; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 303


October 10, 1975, Argued  
August 25, 1976, Decided  
November 1, 1976, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 398 Mich 951.
Rehearing denied by Mich. Canners & Freezers Ass'n v. Agric. Mktg. & Bargaining Bd., 398 Mich. 951, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 1036 (1976)
Jurisdiction noted by Michigan Canners & Freezers Asso. v. Agricultural Marketing & Bargaining Bd., 464 U.S. 912, 104 S. Ct. 271, 78 L. Ed. 2d 252, 1983 U.S. LEXIS 1946 (1983)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mich. Canners & Freezers Ass'n v. Agric. Mktg. & Bargaining Bd., 393 Mich. 788, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 1140 (1975)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to circuit court for consideration of the constitutional and statutory construction issues; jurisdiction retained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association was granted leave to appeal judgments of the Ingham Circuit Court (Michigan) and the Court of Appeals (Michigan), dismissing its action filed to challenge the accreditation under the Michigan Agricultural Marketing and Bargaining Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 290.701 et seq., of a division of appellee marketing association as the sole sales and bargaining representative of a newly created bargaining unit.


OVERVIEW: The association brought an action in circuit court alternatively as a petition for review of a final decision of an administrative agency under the Administrative Procedures Act (APA), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 24.201 et seq., and as an original action seeking an injunction and declaratory ruling on the unconstitutionality and construction of the Michigan Agricultural Marketing and Bargaining Act. The circuit court dismissed the action ruling that all Michigan Agricultural Marketing and Bargaining Board action required review in the court of appeals. The association filed for leave to appeal and a claim of appeal with the court of appeals. Both were denied. The association then filed a petition for review in the court of appeals under § 5(2) of the Act. The court held that there was no reason why the association was not allowed to raise the question of the applicability of the APA to the Act before the circuit court. However, the circuit court could not consider the association's challenge to the validity of the declaration of accreditation of the division on the merits because the court of appeals had original jurisdiction over such an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the circuit court for consideration of the constitutional and statutory construction issues. The court retained appellate jurisdiction over the other issues in the case.

 

334 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Michigan Canners & Freezers Asso. v. Agricultural Marketing & Bargaining Bd.


Docket No. 56434


Supreme Court of Michigan


416 Mich. 706; 332 N.W.2d 134; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 330


October 10, 1975, Argued  
August 25, 1976, Originally decided; December 23, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued after remand June 4, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: Mich. Canners & Freezers Ass'n v. Agric. Mktg. & Bargaining Bd., 393 Mich. 788, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 1140 (1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, organization of handlers of agricultural commodities, individual handlers, and producers, appealed the judgment of the circuit court (Michigan), challenged the constitutionality of the Agricultural Marketing and Bargaining Act (AMABA), and contended that defendant Agricultural Marketing and Bargaining Board (board) failed to comply with the requirements of the Administrative Procedures Act of 1969 (APA).


OVERVIEW: The case was before the court for the second time after being remanded to the circuit court to develop a record. Plaintiffs claimed that AMABA, Mich. Comp. Laws § 290.701 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 12.94(101) et seq.) was pre-empted by the Federal Agricultural Fair Practices Act of 1967 (FAFPA), 7 U.S.C.S. § 2301 et seq. and exceeded the state's police power, that AMABA's provisions exceeded the scope of its title, and that the board failed to comply with the APA when it accredited a division of defendant marketing association. The court held that the APA applied because accreditation proceedings were contested cases and that AMABA was constitutional. The court found that: (1) AMABA was not pre-empted because Congress did not intend to completely occupy the field, AMABA was not an obstacle to the accomplishment and execution of FAFPA's purposes and objectives, and compliance with both acts was not physically impossible; (2) the requirements of due process were satisfied because AMABA addressed a proper public purpose and its remedy was reasonably related to that purpose; and (3) AMABA's title fairly expressed its subject, as required by Mich. Const. art. 4, § 24 (1963).


OUTCOME: The court held that AMABA was constitutional and that the APA applied to accreditation proceedings under AMABA.

 

335 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Negri v. Slotkin


Docket No. 57795


Supreme Court of Michigan


397 Mich. 105; 244 N.W.2d 98; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 297


May 4, 1976, Argued  
July 8, 1976, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Court of Appeals is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party sought review of a decision of a court of appeals (Michigan), which denied his motion for peremptory reversal of a judgment entered in favor of appellees, owner and driver, holding that a state supreme court decision on the constitutionality of the guest passenger act applied only in that particular case as it was decision rendered by less than four justices.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was injured while a guest in a vehicle. Despite plaintiff's objections that the guest passenger act was unconstitutional, the matter was sent to the jury and a judgment of no cause of action was entered based on the trial court's submission of the case to the jury on the guest passenger act's theory of gross negligence and wilful and wanton misconduct only. The court of appeals initially held the matter in abeyance pending the court's decision in a separate case, but then denied plaintiff's motion for peremptory reversal reasoning that the decision reached in that case applied only to that case. The court granted leave to determine whether a decision rendered by less than four justices, who nevertheless constituted a majority of a legally constituted quorum, was binding on the lower courts. It determined that the five justices constituted a quorum and, when three of the five concurred, the judgment stood as valid as any judgment or decree. As such, a three-to-two decision of the court was binding on the court of appeals and the trial courts until overruled by a later decision of the court.


OUTCOME: The court found that its three-to-two decisions were binding on lower tribunals and reversed the decision of the court of appeals, which found that such a judgment applied only to the case in which the judgment was entered.

Craig v. Detroit Police Dep't


Docket No. 55334


Supreme Court of Michigan


397 Mich. 185; 243 N.W.2d 236; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 300


November 7, 1974, Argued  
July 8, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Craig v. Detroit Police Dep't, 49 Mich. App. 599, 212 N.W.2d 235, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 859 (1973)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded to circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed a circuit court judgment holding that it had jurisdiction over the taxpayer's action alleging illegal seizure of property and ordering appellee police department to return funds because the police department failed to follow statutory requirements.


OVERVIEW: The state treasury department prepared jeopardy tax assessments and warrants of levy in the amount of $ 12,985 against the taxpayer under the authority of the Use Tax Act and the Income Tax Act. The state treasury served warrants on four banks and the police department, and, as a result, acquired $ 5,045 toward the taxes due. The taxpayer was then notified of the assessment and brought an action requesting that the state treasury be ordered to show cause why the confiscated funds should not be returned. The appellate court reversed the circuit court's judgment for the taxpayer on the ground that the circuit court had no jurisdiction and that the taxpayer failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. On review, the court reversed and held that the circuit court had jurisdiction because the acts under which the warrants were obtained made no provision for a prompt post-seizure hearing into the factual basis for the assessment. Absent such provision, the circuit court of the county of the residence of the taxpayer provided a logical forum for such a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court that had reversed the circuit court's ruling in the taxpayer's favor, and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Michigan Baptist Homes & Development Co. v. Ann Arbor


Docket No. 56407


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 660; 242 N.W.2d 749; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 278


November 6, 1975, Argued; December 19, 1975, Resubmitted  
June 3, 1976, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff aged home operator sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the denial of plaintiff's claimed tax-exempt status.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff aged home operator challenged the denial of it's claimed tax-exempt status and argued that it was entitled to a statutory exemption from the payment of ad valorem property taxes as property owned and occupied by a benevolent or charitable institution. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court which had denied plaintiff tax-exempt status because the home operated by plaintiff was not occupied for what would traditionally be called charitable or benevolent objectives. The court determined that a charity or benevolence benefitted the general public without restriction and that plaintiff provided a retirement environment for those who were in good health and who could afford to pay for it. The health and financial limitations plaintiff placed upon its residents could not be said to benefit the elderly as a general proposition and it, therefore, was not entitled to tax-exempt status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment that plaintiff aged home operator was not entitled to tax-exempt status for property taxes because the retirement community did not benefit the elderly but rather only those in good health who could afford to pay to live in the community.

People v. Dempster


Docket No. 55703


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 700; 242 N.W.2d 381; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 280; 84 A.L.R.3d 562; 19 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 845


April 9, 1975, Argued  
June 3, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Dempster, 51 Mich. App. 612, 216 N.W.2d 81, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 952 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Conviction reversed and defendant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) that convicted defendants of selling unregistered securities in violation of the Uniform Securities Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 451.701.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of selling unregistered securities in violation of the Uniform Securities Act (Act), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. 451.701. On appeal, defendants argued that the securities were exempt as "commercial paper" from the registration provisions of the statute, that the statute impermissibly placed the burden of proof on defendant to prove an exemption, and that the "commercial paper" exemption was not sufficiently definite to sustain the criminal conviction. The court ruled that the Act granted exemptions from registration only in instances where the securities were riskless, such as government bonds, and the type of instruments sold by defendants were not "commercial paper" within the meaning of the Act. Further, the court held that there was ample evidence that the state met its burden of proof to require defendants to prove the exempt status of the securities. Finally, the court found that while it placed a clear definition upon the commercial paper exemption, the term "commercial paper" standing by itself was not sufficiently definite at the time of the conviction to allow the conviction to stand.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting defendants of securities laws violations was reversed where the unregistered securities sold by defendants were not "commercial paper" within the meaning of applicable securities act. The term "commercial paper" was not sufficiently definite, at the time of the convictions, to sustain a conviction.

People v. Hall


Docket No. 55337


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 650; 242 N.W.2d 377; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 277


June 3, 1975, Argued  
June 3, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Hall, 391 Mich. 786, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 883 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which denied his petition for mandamus to review the trial court's denial of his delayed motion for new trial following his conviction for felony murder.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's conviction for felony murder was affirmed on appeal, he filed a petition for mandamus to review the trial court's denial of his delayed motion for new trial. The appellate court denied his petition. Defendant argued that his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures was violated by forced participation in a lineup while in police custody, that his conviction could not be sustained because it was based solely on untrustworthy, unreliable, and legally insufficient evidence, and that the prosecutor's misconduct denied him a fair trial. The court stated that once an accused was initially restrained by lawful incarceration without infringement of any search and seizure rights, forced participation in a lineup, complete with a speaking requirement, did not constitute an unreasonable search and seizure. Identification testimony of witnesses, if believed by the jury, established defendant as one of the perpetrators of the crime. No objections or requests for curative instructions were made in response to the prosecutor's closing argument, and the court could not agree with defendant that appropriate cautionary instructions would not have cured any error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment, which denied defendant's petition for mandamus to review the trial court's denial of his delayed motion for a new trial.

People v. Stewart


Docket No. 55230


Supreme Court of Michigan


400 Mich. 540; 256 N.W.2d 31; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 228


February 3, 1977, Submitted on Rehearing. July 18, 1977 Decided.  
June 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Argued December 10, 1974 (Calendar No. 5). Decided June 4, 1976, 397 Mich 1. Rehearing Granted 398 Mich 951, December 9, 1976.
People v. Stewart, 397 Mich. 1, 242 N.W.2d 760, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 289 (1976)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to conviction of sale of heroin; reversed as to conviction of possession of heroin.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed his convictions for the sale of heroin and possession of heroin.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the sale of heroin and possession of heroin. Upon review, the appellate court affirmed, and upon further review, the court originally affirmed both convictions. Upon rehearing, the court affirmed the conviction for sale of heroin and reversed the conviction for possession of heroin. The court held that from the evidence adduced at trial, the illegal possession of heroin was obviously a lesser-included offense of the illegal sale of heroin. The court held that when the jury found defendant guilty of the illegal sale of the heroin, they necessarily found him guilty of possession of the same heroin. The court held that the possession and sale clearly constituted one single and same act, thus two convictions for the same act constituted double jeopardy. The court held that defendant could not be doubly punished by convicting him of possession, which in his case was a necessary prerequisite for the very sale for which he was also convicted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for the sale of heroin and reversed his conviction for possession of heroin.

Advisory Opinion on Constitutionality of 1975 PA 227 (Questions 2-10)


Docket No. 57850


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 465; 242 N.W.2d 3; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 328


March 5, 1976, Argued  
May 21, 1976, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Michigan legislature requested the issuance of an advisory opinion regarding the constitutionality of proposed legislation on political reform, 1975 Mich. Pub. Acts 227, to be codified at Mich. Comp. Laws § 169.1 et seq.(Mich. Stat. Ann. § 4.1701(1) et seq.).


OVERVIEW: In response to the legislature's request for an advisory opinion regarding the constitutionality of the political reform act, the court reviewed the legislation and came to the following conclusions: (1) the provision prohibiting communication regarding a sworn complaint before the political ethics commission impermissibly infringed on the freedoms of speech and of the press, (2) the specific organization structure for campaigns was constitutional, but the expenditure limitations for "persons" and the candidate himself or his family were not constitutional, (3) the prohibition on corporate contributions was constitutional for influencing the nomination of a candidate but not for influencing the passage of legislation, (4) financing of state gubernatorial elections was a public purpose for appropriation but it was required to be on a year-to-year basis, (5) requiring disclosure of financial information was not an unconstitutional invasion of privacy for some officials but was overbroad for officials with geographically limited spheres of influence, (6) the oath of office was constitutional, and (7) restrictions on lobbyists were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court determined that some provisions of the proposed legislation would violate the state constitution.

 

342 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Hart v. County of Wayne


Docket No. 57143


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 259; 240 N.W.2d 697; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 256


January 8, 1976, Argued  
April 1, 1976, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed and the summary judgment in favor of the defendant City of Detroit and the intervening defendants Judges of the Recorder's Court of Detroit is reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the judges of the recorder's court and a city, appealed the order of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which found that 1919 Mich. Pub. Acts 369 § 13, Mich. Comp. Laws § 725.13, which created the recorder's court, was invalidly adopted, reversed the award of summary judgment to the judges, and awarded summary judgment to plaintiff taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action to have § 725.13 declared unconstitutional because it was not ratified by local voters as required by Mich. Const. of 1908, Art. 5, § 30 , and to enjoin payment of the judges salaries. The judges intervened. The circuit court awarded summary judgment to the city and the judges. The taxpayer appealed. The appellate court reversed and awarded summary judgment to the taxpayer. The judges appealed. The court reversed. Because the recorder's court performed a state and not a local function, the funding was a legislative function. The state had merely apportioned the public expenses by county which was permissible. Therefore, § 725.13 was not a local act and a referendum of approval was not required. Because the recorder's court absorbed part of the county's case load the charge to the county, which was shared by the city, was reasonable. In addition, the establishment of the courts was given to the legislature to establish by general act in Mich. Const. art. 7, § 1. Therefore, Mich. Const. art. 5, § 10 general subject provisions were inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the appellate court, which had reversed the circuit court's award of summary judgment to the city and the judges, reinstated the circuit court award, and declined to award costs.

Department of Natural Resources v. Seaman


Docket Nos. 55942, 55943, 55944


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 299; 240 N.W.2d 206; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 259


May 7, 1975, Argued  
April 1, 1976, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant fishermen challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed condemnation and confiscation orders issued by the circuit court against the fishermen for acts of illegal fishing. Officials of defendant, the Michigan Department of Natural Resources (DNR), seized the fishermen's vessel after conducting a warrantless search.


OVERVIEW: The court found that § 1b(2) of the Commercial Fishing Law, Mich. Comp. Laws § 308.1b, which authorized the director of conservation to place restrictions on commercial fishing licenses, did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority. The court also found that Dep't Natural Resources Order 17, R. 3, which restricted the number and type of nets to be used by the fishermen, did not exceed the authority granted the DNR by the legislature. The court construed Mich. Comp. Laws § 300.12 as, inter alia, requiring the presence of exigent circumstances before conservation officers were authorized to conduct warrantless searches under the act. The court reversed in part and found that there were not exigent circumstances, where DNR officials had ample time to obtain a valid search warrant. The court concluded that the vessel had to be returned to the fishermen, because property that had been wrongfully seized following an invalid search should be returned to the owner.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the appellate court's decision with respect to the seizure of the vessel. The court affirmed the remainder of the appellate court's judgment and remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings not inconsistent with its opinion.

Reist v. Bay County Circuit Judge


Docket No. 56919


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 326; 241 N.W.2d 55; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 260


June 6, 1975, Argued  
April 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Reist v. Bay Circuit Judge, 394 Mich. 763, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 355 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Remanded to probate court for appointment of counsel and furnishing of transcripts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff indigent mother, who had her parental rights to her two-and-one-half year-old child terminated and her one-year old child made a ward of the state, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court (Michigan), which denied her request for appointment of counsel for her appeal as of right. The indigent mother also sought a transcript of the court's proceedings to be provided at public expense, which terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The indigent mother requested appointment of counsel for her appeal as of right to the circuit court and asked that a transcript of the trial court's proceedings be provided at public expense. Both the trial court and the circuit court denied her requests. On appeal, the court determined that the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Michigan Constitutions required that transcripts and counsel be furnished at public expense to an indigent parent desiring to appeal as of right a decision terminating parental rights. The court concluded that the rule requiring the appointment of counsel to represent indigent parents at hearings that involved termination of their parental rights was constitutionally based. JCR 1969, 6.3(A)(2)(b). Because of the nature of parental rights termination proceedings and of the parental relationship, the court held that the Due Process Clause required the assignment of counsel at public expense for hearings when the state sought to terminate parental rights.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the trial court for the entry of an order appointing counsel for the indigent mother and directed that appointed counsel be furnished transcripts of the neglect and termination proceedings. The court held that appointed counsel could appeal as of right to the circuit court within two weeks of appointment.

Dow v. State


Docket No. 54848


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 192; 240 N.W.2d 450; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 250


March 12, 1974, Argued  
April 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Dow v. State, 46 Mich. App. 101, 207 N.W.2d 441, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1178 (1973)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded to the trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers and buyers filed a suit against the state to quiet title in certain of the taxpayer and buyers' property that was acquired by the state in a tax sale for violation of the Due Process Clause of the U.S. Const. amend. I in connection with the sale. The Circuit Court (Michigan) held that the statutory requirements concerning tax sales had been complied with and entered a judgment for the state. The taxpayers and buyers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers held title to certain property in which they owed a tax deficiency and which they sold to the buyers on a land contract. Proceedings to foreclose a tax lien were initiated and notice was provided to the taxpayers in a publication in a city in which neither the taxpayers nor the buyers resided. The state purchased the property at a tax sale and did not provide the buyer with notice to redeem. The taxpayers and buyers argued the tax sale was defective because of inadequate notice of the tax foreclosure proceedings pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. §§ 211.62, 211.63, 211.66 (Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 7.107, 7.108, 7.111).The court held (1) the Due Process Clause applied because the taxpayers and buyers had a significant property interest in the real estate; (2) they were entitled to an opportunity to be heard at a meaningful time and in a meaningful manner and to notice reasonably calculated to apprise them of such opportunity; (3) the state was required to employ reasonable means to notify them of the proceedings; (4) notice could be by mail or by publication; and (5) notice by publication was not constitutionally adequate because their names and addresses were known.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment for the state and remanded to the circuit court for entry of a judgment quieting title in the taxpayers, subject to the buyers' interest pursuant to the land contract.

State ex rel. Cahalan v. Diversified Theatrical Corp.


Docket Nos. 56964, 56965


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 244; 240 N.W.2d 460; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 254


November 7, 1975, Argued  
April 1, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: State ex rel. Cahalan v. Diversified Theatrical Corp., 59 Mich. App. 223, 229 N.W.2d 389, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1341 (1975)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Court of Appeals (Michigan) found for plaintiff prosecutor and held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.3801, which provided that a place of lewdness, assignation or prostitution was a public nuisance, could be properly applied to defendant motion picture theatre. The theater appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The lower court held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.3801, which provided that a place of lewdness, assignation, or prostitution was a public nuisance, was applicable to the motion picture theatre because it showed films that were obscene under state and federal constitutional standards. The court held that § 600.3801 was intended to apply to houses of prostitution and not to motion picture theatres where sexual acts were not committed but were portrayed on the screen. The statute was enacted to subject houses of prostitution to abatement as nuisances and was not intended to regulate the morals of private individuals. The meaning of the words "lewdness, assignation, or prostitution" was clear in light of the history and purpose of the statutes and that meaning could not properly be expanded by judicial construction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that held that a statute providing that a place of lewdness was a public nuisance could be applied to a motion picture theatre.

In re Advisory Opinion: etc.


Docket No. 57850


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 123; 240 N.W.2d 193; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 327


March 5, 1976, Argued  
March 29, 1976, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Statute declared unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At the request of the House of Representatives, the court considered the constitutionality of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. §§ 169.1-169.200, Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 4.1701(1)-4.1701(200), which created the Political Ethics Commission as an autonomous entity within the Department of State. The issue was whether the statute offended the provisions of Mich. Const. art. 4, § 24 (1963).


OVERVIEW: At the request of the House of Representatives, the court considered whether Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 169.1-169.200, Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 4.1701(1)-4.1701(200), which created the Political Ethics Commission (commission) as an autonomous entity within the Department of State, was unconstitutional under the provisions of Mich. The statute created the commission, provided requirements for the establishment of candidate committees, provided for the filing of statements of organization and reporting, set maximum limits on expenditures by candidates, established a fund for distribution to qualifying gubernatorial candidates, proscribed conflicts of interest, required financial disclosures, required the registration and reporting of lobbying activities, and provided for the repeal of five existing laws. The court held that the prohibition against the passage of an act relating to different objects expressed in the title made the whole act void, and many of the provisions of the statute had no necessary connection with each other.


OUTCOME: The court decreed that the statute was unconstitutional.

349 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Howell


Docket Nos. 55799, 56180


Supreme Court of Michigan


396 Mich. 16; 238 N.W.2d 148; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 230


April 8, 1975, Argued; June 5, 1975, Argued  
January 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Helzer, 54 Mich. App. 285, 220 N.W.2d 735, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1235 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The case of defendant Howell is remanded for trial and defendant Helzer's conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), defendants, one of whom was charged with assault with intent to commit gross indecency and the other of whom was convicted of committing an act of gross indecency, challenged the constitutionality of the statutes on the basis of vagueness. The state appealed the appellate court's decision that had overturned the second defendant's conviction.


OVERVIEW: The first defendant was charged with forcing an adult female to perform an act of fellatio in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.85, and the second defendant was convicted of stroking the penis of and performing fellatio upon a minor in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.338. The court noted that because the challenges did not involve First Amendment freedoms, the statutes were to be examined in the light of the facts of the case. While the term "act of gross indecency" standing alone failed to give adequate notice of the conduct proscribed, the statutes gave defendants adequate notice that the conduct they engaged in was illegal. The court construed "act of gross indecency" to prohibit oral and manual sexual acts committed without consent or with a person under the age of consent. Finally, the trial court did not err when it instructed the jury that the date the offense was committed was not a material element of the offense. Only a single incident was alleged, and therefore the jury could not have convicted the second defendant of some other act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision insofar as it reversed the second defendant's conviction for committing an act of gross indecency. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment insofar as it declined to hold the respective statutes vague. The court remanded the first defendant's case for trial.

Bundo v. Walled Lake


Docket No. 55935


Supreme Court of Michigan


395 Mich. 679; 238 N.W.2d 154; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 287


March 5, 1975, Argued  
January 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Bundo v. Walled Lake, 53 Mich. App. 317, 218 N.W.2d 869, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1143 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The cause is remanded for further action not inconsistent with the opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bar owner appealed a decision of the Michigan Court of Appeals, which affirmed summary judgment to defendants, the Michigan Liquor Control Commission (MLCC) and a city, in the owner's complaint that disputed the city's recommendation to the MLCC, which refused to renew the owner's liquor license under § 17, Mich. Comp. Laws § 436.17 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.988), of the Michigan Liquor Control Act (MLCA).


OVERVIEW: After receiving three renewals of his liquor license from the MLCC, the owner had allowed topless dancing in his bar. Under the MLCA, the city's recommendation compelled the MLCC to refuse to renew the owner's license, without notification or a hearing. On appeal, the court affirmed that the nature of the entertainment was irrelevant to the issue of whether the owner was entitled procedural due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Mich. Const. art. I, § 40. The court rejected arguments by the city and the MLCC because recent case law distinguished property rights from a government granted privileges. The court found that the owner's interest in obtaining a renewal of his license was akin to the vested property interest of a tenured government employee. The court concluded that the owner, who obtained and renewed his license and had reasonably relied upon the practice that provided for renewal as a matter of course, was entitled to rudimentary due process protection with some modification. The court reversed the appellate court and held that the courts had the authority to review the refusal because the actions of the city were arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower appellate court's determination that the state courts had no authority to review the decision of the city and the MLCC to refuse a liquor license to the owner. The court remanded for rudimentary due process procedures prior to a recommendation by the city to the MLCC.

 

351 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Bisco's, Inc. v. Michigan Liquor Control Com.


Docket No. 55952


Supreme Court of Michigan


395 Mich. 706; 238 N.W.2d 166; 1976 Mich. LEXIS 288


March 5, 1975, Argued  
January 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Bisco's, Inc. v. Mich. Liquor Control Comm'n, 392 Mich. 755, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 686 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals (Michigan) which dismissed the licensee's complaint for mandamus, holding that it was precluded from reviewing the village's action that recommended to the appellee Michigan Liquor Control Commission (commission) that the license not be renewed and the commission's decision not to renew licensee's liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The commission issued a liquor license to the licensee with a dance entertainment permit. The village approved the issuance of the license. Subsequently, the licensee began topless dancing entertainment and the village filed an objection with the commission to the renewal of the licensee's liquor license. Pursuant to the village's objection, the commission advised the licensee that its license would not be renewed. The licensee sought review in the circuit court, which concluded it did not have jurisdiction to issue an order to the commission. The licensee then filed a complaint for mandamus with the court of appeals, which declined to order the village to withdraw its objection to the commission to renew the license. The court of appeals dismissed the complaint, holding that it was precluded from reviewing a local legislative body's action with respect to approval of liquor licenses. The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals, finding that the licensee had a property interest in the liquor license and that the Due Process Clause required that the licensee be afforded an opportunity for an evidentiary hearing prior to nonrenewal of its license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals and remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion requiring that the licensee be afforded an evidentiary hearing prior to the commission's decision not to renew the liquor license. The court also concluded that on remand, the court of appeals should determined whether the village was properly joined as a party defendant.

Northview Constr. Co. v. St. Clair Shores


Docket No. 54712


Supreme Court of Michigan


395 Mich. 497; 236 N.W.2d 396; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 180


March 14, 1974, Argued  
December 18, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing granted 395 Mich 924.
Rehearing granted by Northview Constr. Co. v. City of St Clair Shores, 395 Mich. 924, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 387 (1976)
Affirmed by, On rehearing at Northview Constr. Co. v. St. Clair Shores, 399 Mich. 184, 249 N.W.2d 290, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 212 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Northview Constr. Co. v. St. Clair Shores, 44 Mich. App. 614, 205 N.W.2d 895, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1035 (1973)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff builders filed a class action against defendant city for illegally excessive building permit fees. The builders sought review of the order of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the class action on remand.


OVERVIEW: City's building code established an illegally excessive building permit fee schedule. Builders filed an action against the city to secure a refund of the excess fees paid by the builders and all excess fees paid by a class of persons who purchased building permits. The trial court dismissed the class action portion and entered judgment in favor of the builders. The appellate court reversed and remanded for proper notice. Only six additional builders responded to the notice. The court held that: 1) there was no support in the record for a conclusion that the builders' acceptance of individual judgments rendered them inadequate class representatives; 2) the appellate court and the trial court erred when they relied on the small number of intervening class members to find there was insufficient interest to continue the class action; 3) the notice provided to the absent class members was inadequate and the lower courts lacked a sufficient factual basis upon which to measure the interest of the class members; and 4) there was not sufficient evidence to support the finding of inadequacy of representation based on the conduct of the builders or the small number of intervenors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment dismissing the builders' class action and remanded to the trial court for a resolution of the class claims.

Keating International Corp. v. Orion


Docket No. 55668


Supreme Court of Michigan


395 Mich. 539; 236 N.W.2d 409; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 182


January 7, 1975, Argued  
December 18, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Keating International Corp. v. Orion, 51 Mich. App. 122, 214 N.W.2d 551, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 885 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developers appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed a trial court's order compelling approval of the developers' site plan that defendant planning commission had denied.


OVERVIEW: The developers' land parcels were zoned multiple residential when they filed site plans for multiple development with the planning commission. In response to the commission's and the home owners association's objections, the developers modified the proposal several times before bringing an action seeking a writ of mandamus to compel approval of the plan, money damages, and a show cause order. Nearly two months later, at a public hearing, the property was rezoned single-family residential. The developers then filed an amended complaint requesting a permanent injunction against the commission's interference with the designated use assigned to the parcels zoned multiple residential. The trial court denied the motion, but ruled that rezoning would be inadmissible at trial. After trial, the trial court issued an order compelling approval of the plan. The appellate court affirmed. The court further affirmed, concluding that it was not error for the trial court to exclude the amended zoning ordinance from the case because the judge viewed the commission's actions as showing bad faith and unjustified delay and the record was void of competent evidence to support the rejection of the plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order compelling approval of the land developers' site plan.

In re Request for Advisory Opinion, etc.


Docket No. 57623


Supreme Court of Michigan


395 Mich. 148; 235 N.W.2d 321; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 288



November 25, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Request for Advisory Opinion on 1975 Pa 227, 395 Mich. 910, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 802 (1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The clerk of the Michigan House of Representatives requested an advisory opinion from the court regarding 1975 Mich. Pub. Acts 227.


OVERVIEW: The clerk sent a letter to the court and called its attention to § 200 of 1975 Mich. Pub. Acts 227. The court interpreted the letter as a request for an advisory opinion. Viewed against what the state Constitution required, the court held that § 200 was insufficient to invoke the court's discretionary power to render an advisory opinion. The request did not specify the "important questions of law" upon which the House of Representatives wished the court to speak. In addition, the court noted that the request was made during the enactment process itself, whereas the Constitution required that the request be made after enactment and before the effective date.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request for an advisory opinion without prejudice.

Regents of University of Mich. v. State


Docket No. 54966


Supreme Court of Michigan


395 Mich. 52; 235 N.W.2d 1; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 154


May 7, 1974, Argued  
October 28, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Regents of University of Mich. v. State, 47 Mich. App. 23, 208 N.W.2d 871, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1266 (1973)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Michigan and intervening defendant Michigan State Board of Education (board) sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the trial court's decision that 1971 Mich. Pub. Acts 122 (act), §§ 13, 20 and 28 were unconstitutional, and found that Mich. Const. art. VIII, § 3 (1963) did not require that universities obtain prior board approval to expand or establish programs or campuses.


OVERVIEW: The universities claimed that the act infringed upon their constitutional autonomy by limiting the number of out-of-state students, limiting raises in tuition, and unduly restricting the operation of higher learning institutions. The board claimed that the universities had to obtain the board's approval for implementation of new programs. The court affirmed, as modified, the judgment of the lower appellate court. The court held that §§ 13 and 28 and the first sentence of § 20 of the act were technically moot and did not address those issues. The second sentence of § 20 was constitutional in that its requirement that the universities submit schedules for the liquidation of certain debt was a mere reporting measure and there was no requirement for legislative approval. The court abstained on ruling on the third sentence of § 20, which precluded the use of operating funds for self-liquidating projects, because no specific impasse was presented. The court held that under Mich. Const. art. VIII, § 3, the board had no dominating authority over the universities. The universities were required to inform the board of new programs; however, the board had no power to veto the programs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower appellate court to the extent that it was not inconsistent with the court's opinion regarding the constitutionality of legislation concerning the universities.

 

356 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Manistee Bank & Trust Co. v. McGowan


Docket No. 54961


Supreme Court of Michigan


394 Mich. 655; 232 N.W.2d 636; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 266


May 8, 1974, Argued  
September 8, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Manistee Bank & Trust Co. v. McGowan, 390 Mich. 795, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 671 (1973)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator brought an action against appellee driver after the administrator's decedent was killed in an automobile accident. The trial court (Michigan) denied the administrator's motion to strike that portion of the driver's answer relying on the guest passenger exception, Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.401; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 9.2101. The jury returned a verdict of no cause of action. The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The jury returned a verdict of no cause of action because the driver was guilty only of ordinary negligence. The guest passenger exception provided that guests transported in motor vehicles could not recover against the owner or driver absent a showing of gross negligence or wilful and wanton misconduct. The administrator argued that the guest passenger exception was unconstitutional. The court agreed and held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.401; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 9.2101 was unconstitutional as violative of the Equal Protection Clause of Mich. Const. art. I, § 2 (1963). The court concluded that the classifications which the guest passenger exception created did not bear a substantial and rational relation to the statute's purposes of protecting the hospitality of the host-driver and of preventing collusive lawsuits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court on the question of damages.

Nickola v. Grand Blanc


Docket No. 55088


Supreme Court of Michigan


394 Mich. 589; 232 N.W.2d 604; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 261


June 7, 1974, Argued  
August 19, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Nickola v. Grand Blanc, 47 Mich. App. 684, 209 N.W.2d 803, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1349 (1973)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed the trial court's decision in favor of the township in plaintiff landowners' challenge of the township's zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The landowners purchased property, which was zoned for single residences, to build a mobile-home park. The township refused to grant the landowners' petition for rezoning. Under the township's master plan, adopted after the rejection of the petition, mobile-home parks were placed in areas of transitional land use. The landowners brought an action against the township, challenging its zoning ordinance. The court affirmed the lower court's reversal of the trial court's judgment in favor of the township. The court found that the landowners failed to overcome the presumption that the township's residential zoning of their property was valid. However, the township's unreasonable exclusion of mobile-home parks made its zoning ordinance invalid. The court noted that all applications for new parks had been denied since 1959 and that only one of the existing parks had been allowed to expand. Further, the transitional use area did not call for municipal sewer and water services. Therefore, the virtual exclusion of the parks was unreasonable and without justification, based on the availability of land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's reversal of the trial court's decision in favor of the township. The case was remanded to the trial court.

Dearborn Fire Fighters Union v. Dearborn


Docket Nos. 54308, 54309


Supreme Court of Michigan


394 Mich. 229; 231 N.W.2d 226; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 225; 90 L.R.R.M. 2002; 77 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P53,740


June 5, 1973, Argued  
June 24, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing denied 395 Mich 901.
Rehearing denied by Dearborn Fire Fighters Union v. City of Dearborn, 395 Mich. 901, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 797 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Dearborn Fire Fighters Union Local No. 412, IAFF v. City of Dearborn, 42 Mich. App. 51, 201 N.W.2d 650, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 888 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant City of Dearborn appealed a decision from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), that ordered enforcement of decisions under Mich. Comp. Laws § 423.231 et seq., Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.455(31) et seq. which provided for compulsory arbitration of police and fire department labor disputes, as requested by plaintiff unions.


OVERVIEW: The lower court ordered the city to enforce decisions from arbitration initiated by the police and firemen unions pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 423.231 et seq., Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.455(31) et seq., (Act) which provided for compulsory arbitration of police and fire department labor disputes. The city appealed. The court found the Act unconstitutional. The arbitrator/chairman of the panel was entrusted with the authority to decide major questions of public policy concerning the conditions of public employment, the levels and standards of public services, and the allocation of public revenues. Those questions were legislative and political, not judicial or quasi-judicial. The Act was structured to insulate the arbitrator/chairman's decision from review in the political process. It was not intended that he be, nor was he in fact, accountable within the political process for his decision. This was not consonant with the constitutional exercise of political power in a representative democracy. The court gave the ruling prospective effect. Orders of arbitration panels heretofore entered were enforced, because the arbitration panels proceeded in accordance with the Act.


OUTCOME: The court held the statute in question unconstitutional with prospective application. The court ordered enforcement of the decisions of the arbitration panels previously entered; the court thus affirmed the decisions of the lower court granting enforcement of the arbitration orders.

Cochrane v. Westwood Wholesale Grocery Co.


Docket No. 55572


Supreme Court of Michigan


394 Mich. 164; 229 N.W.2d 309; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 214


November 4, 1974, Argued  
May 27, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Cochrane v. Westwood Wholesale Grocery Co., 391 Mich. 774, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 497 (1974)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The order quashing the writ of garnishment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed an order of an appellate court (Michigan), which found in favor of defendant owner and quashed the claimant's writ of garnishment as unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The claimant filed a garnishment action against the owner under Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.4011. A pre-judgment writ of garnishment was issued as to the owner's funds. The claimant, who had no interest in the funds, was not required to post a bond. The appellate court granted the owner's motion to quash the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment, concluding that the pre-judgment garnishment procedure violated due process under recent United States Supreme Court precedent. That was so because the procedure permitted attachment without a bond or an expedited hearing process to test the merits of a claim. Both were necessary to protect the owner's interests. Further discussion or analysis might cloud the clear rules established by precedent. Accordingly, the court affirmed and remanded for an order consistent with its findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's order, which granted the owner's motion to quash the claimant's writ of garnishment. The matter was remanded for an order consistent with the court's findings.

In re Advisory Opinion Re Constitutionality of 1974 PA 242


Docket No. 56354


Supreme Court of Michigan


394 Mich. 41; 228 N.W.2d 772; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 287


January 8, 1975, Argued  
April 29, 1975, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Michigan senate requested an advisory opinion on the constitutionality of 1974 PA Laws 242 (Law), which dealt with providing aid to schools.


OVERVIEW: The state senate requested the court to give an advisory opinion on the Law. The court determined that the scope of review was limited to whether the Law was constitutional in relation to Mich. Const. of 1963, art. 8, § 2, and further whether it directly or indirectly aided or maintained a nonpublic school. The court held that the textbooks and supplies were essential aids that constituted a primary feature of the educational process and a primary element required for any school to exist, and that § 2 barred public funding for primary and essential elements of a private school's existence. The court accordingly read the law to apply only to public school students and upheld its constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court rendered an advisory opinion that the Law applied only to public schools and was therefore constitutional.

People v. Downes


Docket No. 55308


Supreme Court of Michigan


394 Mich. 17; 228 N.W.2d 212; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 201


November 5, 1974, Argued  
April 29, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Downes, 49 Mich. App. 532, 212 N.W.2d 314, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 851 (1973)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed his conviction under § 7 of the Uniform Narcotic Drug Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.51 et seq. (1937), superceded by the Controlled Substances Act of 1971, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.301 et seq., for prescribing narcotic drugs to certain persons known to be addicts, otherwise than in good faith and in the course of his professional practice.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a doctor, was convicted of prescribing significant quantities of narcotic drugs to addicts and narcotics users in violation of § 7 of the Uniform Narcotic Drug Act (Act). In spite of evidence tending to show that defendant's actions were directed toward a cure, the jury found that defendant was prescribing the drugs other than in good faith and outside of the course of his professional practice. The intermediate court affirmed the conviction. On appeal, the court found that the trial court committed reversible error in failing to instruct the jury that under the Act, the term "good faith" focused on the state of mind and intentions of defendant. It was a subjective standard. The court found that the term "good faith" had a well-defined and generally understood meaning and was not unconstitutionally vague or indefinite.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the defendant's conviction and remanded the case for a new trial.

 

363 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Beavers


Docket No. 54847


Supreme Court of Michigan


393 Mich. 554; 227 N.W.2d 511; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 276


May 10, 1974, Argued  
April 7, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Michigan v. Beavers, 423 U.S. 878, 96 S. Ct. 152, 46 L. Ed. 2d 111, 1975 U.S. LEXIS 2874 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Beavers, 390 Mich. 773, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 391 (1973)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed defendant's conviction for sale of heroin.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the sale of heroin, the lower court affirmed the conviction, and the court reversed the lower court's decision and remanded the case for a new trial. The court held that a search warrant should have been issued prior to instituting that specific participant monitoring procedure because such an investigatory action constituted a search and seizure that could be justified under the state constitution only with a valid search warrant. The court found a significant distinction between assuming the risk that communications directed to one party may subsequently be repeated to others and the simultaneous monitoring of a conversation by the uninvited ear of a third party functioning in cooperation with one of the participants yet unknown to the other. The court held that defendant did not knowingly expose to the public his alleged conversation with the informant, which took place in defendant's own residence. The court further held that the search and seizure was unreasonable and its fruits were inadmissible at trial. The court found that the burden of justification through an exception from the warrant requirement had not been carried.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's decision, which affirmed defendant's conviction for sale of heroin.

Rockwell v. Board of Education


Docket No. 56618


Supreme Court of Michigan


393 Mich. 616; 227 N.W.2d 736; 1975 Mich. LEXIS 283; 89 L.R.R.M. 2017; 77 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P53,693


March 4, 1975, Argued  
April 4, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied 394 Mich   .
Rehearing denied by Rockwell v. Crestwood Sch. Dist. Bd. of Educ., 394 Mich. 944, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 822 (1975)
Appeal dismissed by Crestwood Education Asso. v. Board of Education, 427 U.S. 901, 96 S. Ct. 3184, 49 L. Ed. 2d 1195, 1976 U.S. LEXIS 2213 (1976)
Motion denied by Rockwell v. Crestwood Sch. Dist. Bd. Educ., 399 Mich. 1045, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1488 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: 57 Mich App 636, 226 NW2d 596 (1975).
Rockwell v. Board of Education, 57 Mich. App. 636, 226 N.W.2d 596, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1645 (1975)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school board sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which held that teachers who participated in a strike in violation of the Public Employment Relations Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 423.201 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.455(1) et seq.), could not be terminated without a prior hearing as required by The Teachers' Tenure Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 38.71 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 15.1971 et seq.).


OVERVIEW: Following a labor dispute between appellee union and the school board, teachers instigated a strike. As a result, the board terminated the striking teachers without first providing the hearings required by The Teachers' Tenure Act (Act), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 38.71 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 15.1971 et seq.). Consequently, the teachers' union filed a lawsuit, and the court of appeals held that the teachers, who had participated in the strike in violation of the Public Employment Relations Act (PERA), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 423.201 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.455(1) et seq.), could not be terminated without first holding the hearings required by the Act. The board appealed the ruling. The court reversed. After finding that the teachers were striking public employees under the PERA and that the PERA governed notwithstanding any other law, the court held the striking teachers, who had violated the PERA, could be disciplined under the PERA without a prior hearing despite the Act's requirements. However, the court held the teachers would be entitled to reinstatement if the Michigan Employment Relations Commission determined appellant had engaged in an unfair labor practice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment holding teachers who participated in a strike in violation of the Public Employment Relations Act (PERA) could not be terminated without a prior hearing as required by The Teachers' Tenure Act (Act) because the teachers' strike was covered by the PERA and the PERA preempted the Act. However, the teachers were entitled to reinstatement upon a finding that the school board committed an unfair labor practice.

People v. Milton


Docket No. 55466


Supreme Court of Michigan


393 Mich. 234; 224 N.W.2d 266; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 229


October 11, 1974, Submitted  
December 19, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: People v. Milton, 391 Mich. 817, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 246 (1974)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan) that affirmed his conviction of second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction of second-degree murder. The appellate court affirmed the conviction in an unreported memorandum opinion. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court decision. The court found that, following his arrest, defendant was bound over by a district court to circuit court for trial. Defendant asserted that 1968 Mich. Pub. Acts 154, creating the district court and providing whatever jurisdiction it might have to bind over felons, violated Mich. Const. art 4, § 24 (1963), the title-body clause. The court held, however, that the district court did not violate the title-body clause. The court found that the legislature specifically provided for the court's jurisdiction in criminal matters and specifically covered at least two evidentiary questions arising in criminal cases. The court held that it could not properly ascribe to the legislature an intent to confine the Judicature Act strictly to civil matters.Therefore, the court held that 1968 Mich. Pub. Acts 154 did not violate § 24.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an appellate court decision that affirmed defendant's conviction of second-degree murder.

 

366 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Schwartz v. Secretary of State


Docket No. 56,260


Supreme Court of Michigan


393 Mich. 42; 222 N.W.2d 517; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 211


October 11, 1974, Submitted  
October 30, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Jurisdiction taken by Supreme Court of original action for mandamus in the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner interested resident brought a petition for a discretionary writ of mandamus to compel defendants, Secretary of State and county clerk, to hold an election for the judgeship in one of two new districts created by the legislature at a general election instead of carrying over current municipal judges.


OVERVIEW: With the enactment of Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.9934 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.9934), the legislature transformed five municipal courts with five judges into two district courts with three judges. Therefore, the resident requested that the judgeship of one of the new district courts be filled through an election. The resident based his complaint on Mich. Const. of 1963, art. VI, § 23, as amended, which stated that whenever a new office of judge was created in the district court, the position needed to be filled by an election. As a result, the court applied rules of constitutional interpretation and held that an examination of the "common understanding" as well as the "circumstances" and "purposes" attendant upon the passage of Mich. Const. of 1963, art. VI, § 23, as amended, demonstrated that the legislature had not exceeded its authority. In addition, the court applied the final rule of constitutional construction that whenever possible, an interpretation that did not create constitutional invalidity was preferred. Accordingly, the court denied the writ after determining that the resident had not made out a case for the exercise of a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court denied the resident's request for a writ of mandamus calling for an election.

People v. McQuillan


Docket No. 54,613


Supreme Court of Michigan


392 Mich. 511; 221 N.W.2d 569; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 193


April 3, 1974, Submitted  
September 6, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Horace W. Gilmore, J., and from Court of Appeals prior to decision.



DISPOSITION: Remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution challenged an order from the Wayne Circuit Court (Michigan), which vacated an order that committed defendant for an indeterminate period to the state mental health department and found defendant sane.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found defendant not guilty of assault with intent to rape and indecent liberties by reason of insanity and automatically committed him for an indeterminate period to the state mental health department. Upon defendant's subsequent motion, the trial court vacated the order of commitment. The prosecution appealed the granting of defendant's motion and the trial court's finding of insanity. The court ruled that the trial court's order in favor of defendant would be affirmed if the prosecution did not begin commitment proceedings in probate court within a certain time period. The court held the trial court properly assumed jurisdiction to review the constitutionality of the automatic commitment statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 767.27b (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.966(12)). The court also held that neither due process nor equal protection prohibited a period of temporary statutory detention for examination and observation of one found not guilty by reason of insanity. The court further held, however, that defendant was entitled, upon completion of the examination and observation, to the benefit of commitment and release provisions equal to those given to potential civil committees.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the order vacating the order that committed defendant for an indeterminate period would be affirmed if the prosecution did not begin commitment proceedings in probate court within a certain time period.

 

368 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Bigelow v. Walraven


Docket Nos. 54,920, 54,921


Supreme Court of Michigan


392 Mich. 566; 221 N.W.2d 328; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 195


May 8, 1974, Submitted  
September 6, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 3, Fitzgerald, P. J., and R. B. Burns and Holbrook, JJ., denying application for leave to appeal from Saginaw, Hazen R. Armstrong, J.
Bigelow v. Walraven, 390 Mich. 764, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 564 (1973)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured parties added the board of road commissioners (board) as a defendant six years after they initiated an action against other defendants to recover for injuries received in a car accident. A default was entered against the board. The trial court (Michigan) issued an order setting aside the default on the condition that the board plead to the merits and not plead the statute of limitations defenses. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court granted leave to appeal in order to consider the single question of the propriety of the trial court's conditional order. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion in the instant case because the condition it imposed bore no relationship to any adverse consequence suffered by the injured parties as a result of the board's default. The condition did not restore the injured parties to the position they would have been in had the board timely answered, but rather placed them in a vastly superior position. The trial court erroneously equated the "default" of the injured parties to commence their action against the board until eight years after the accident with the default of the board in failing to answer within 20 days, a lapse it sought to rectify 14 days after entry of the default. The court found that the board advanced a reasonable excuse for failure to comply with the requirements which created the default, and the court concluded that the board should be given an opportunity to defend.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order to the extent that it precluded the board from asserting statute of limitations defenses. The court remanded the case for trial.

State Hwy. Comm'n v. Vanderkloot

Supreme Court of Michigan


392 Mich. 159; 220 N.W.2d 416; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 173; 4 ELR 20694; 6 ERC (BNA) 2006


October 3, 1973, Submitted

OVERVIEW: Appellee Michigan State Highway Commission, acting under authority of the highway condemnation act, commenced condemnation proceedings for the purpose of acquiring land to improve and replace portions of a highway. OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

 

370 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Detroit


Docket No. 54,714


Supreme Court of Michigan


392 Mich. 30; 219 N.W.2d 41; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 167


April 4, 1974, Submitted  
June 25, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 2, 1974.
Later proceeding at Alexander v. Detroit, 154 Mich. App. 722, 398 N.W.2d 508, 1986 Mich. App. LEXIS 2888 (1986)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, Quinn, P. J., and V. J. Brennan and O'Hara, JJ., reversing Wayne, George T. Martin, J.

 45 Mich App 7.
Alexander v. Detroit, 45 Mich. App. 7, 205 N.W.2d 819, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1050 (1973)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class of residents of multiple dwellings (class) appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed the trial court judgment and held that a refuse collection ordinance, Detroit, Mich. Ordinance No. 442-G, was constitutional and not violative of equal protection. The class brought suit against defendant city for exemplary damages.


OVERVIEW: Detroit, Mich. Ordinance No. 442-G provided that multiple dwellings of more than four units were classified as commercial waste and charged higher rates. The court held that inclusion of multiple dwellings with more than four units in the fee-paying "commercial waste" category, while multiple dwellings with four or less units and condominiums and cooperative were excluded, was a constitutionally improper classification violative of the Mich. Const. art. I, § 1 (1963) and the U.S. Const. art. XIV, § 1. The court reasoned that the city did not incur any greater expense in collecting refuse from multiple dwellings with four or more units than from condominiums or cooperatives. The court also held that the class was not estopped from complaining about the city ordinance because they "voluntarily" chose to comply with its terms. The city could not make the class the victims of an unfair classification and then turn around and claim that the class was estopped from complaining because they continued to make payments while fighting their case. The trial judge also did not err in not awarding exemplary damages. There was no proof of the city's willful or malicious conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals and reinstated the trial court's judgment. The city's refuse collection ordinance was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds due to its improper discriminatory classification of the class.
