Central Advertising Co. v. Ann Arbor


Docket Nos. 54,310, 54,311, 54,312, 54,313, 54,316


Supreme Court of Michigan


391 Mich. 533; 218 N.W.2d 27; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 152


September 6, 1973, Submitted  
May 21, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 25, 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Quinn, P. J., and J. W. Fitzgerald and Van Valkenburg, JJ., reversing in part and affirming in part Washtenaw, Paul R. Mahinske, J.

 42 Mich App 59.
Central Advertising Co. v. Ann Arbor, 42 Mich. App. 59, 201 N.W.2d 365, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 889 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Remanded to trial court for specific factfinding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff billboard owners claimed in consolidated proceedings that certain provisions of the Ann Arbor Sign Ordinance (ordinance) were unreasonable or unreasonable as applied to them and that the ordinance constituted an unconstitutional exercise of the police power. Defendant city challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Michigan), which granted relief to the owners and declared the ordinance unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the ordinance's diverse restrictions effectively outlawed billboards. The court determined that the trial court's opinion swept as broadly as the ordinance it condemned. While some provisions of the sign ordinance might have been unreasonable, it was doubtful whether every sign restriction in the ordinance could properly have been said to be unreasonable or unreasonable as applied to the separate owners. The court continued that it was not apparent which of the owners were adversely affected by the "unreasonable" provisions of the ordinance referred to in the trial court's opinion or how many might have been similarly situated. The court was presented with a record concerning a number of issues undifferentiated by fact-finding and with briefs that made no reference to evidence that would support and counter specific findings. Because the court was precluded from deciding an abstract, generalized controversy without supporting evidence, it deferred decision. The case was remanded for further fact-finding so that the court could then appraise the reasonableness of the ordinance's provisions in the context of the facts as they affected the individual owners.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the action for specific fact-finding and direct report to it on the record already made, supplemented as the parties desired, and further briefing after such fact-finding.

People v. Jackson

Supreme Court of Michigan


391 Mich. 323; 217 N.W.2d 22; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 139


November 8, 1973, Submitted

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division 1 (Michigan), which rejected his assignments of error from his conviction for assault with intent to rob being armed in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.89, except as to the assignments that related to identification procedures, and remanded to the trial court for an independent origin determination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested when he tried to use a stolen credit card from an earlier armed robbery. He pleaded guilty to the credit card charge. He was convicted for the armed robbery by the same trial court that had accepted his guilty plea. The main issue in the case was identification. It made its ruling retroactive to defendant and remanded with instructions that a different trial court be assigned to the case.

People v. Moore


Docket No. 54,651


Supreme Court of Michigan


391 Mich. 426; 216 N.W.2d 770; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 145


January 11, 1974, Submitted  
April 16, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, McGregor, P. J., and Bronson and Targonski, JJ., affirming Genesee, Philip C. Elliott, J.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of unlawful possession of a narcotic drug. He was sentenced by the trial court to serve a prison term of eight to ten years. The Michigan Court of Appeals, Division 1, in an unpublished per curiam opinion, affirmed, and reduced the minimum term to six years and eight months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted after a jury trial of unlawful possession of a narcotic drug and sentenced to eight to ten years imprisonment. The appellate court reduced the minimum to six years and eight months. Defendant claimed that he received ineffective assistance of counsel and that evidence was seized from him unlawfully. The court affirmed the lower court's conviction but remanded for resentencing. The court held that where the record showed that the sentencing court considered a conviction that was invalid under Gideon, an appellate court would remand for resentencing. The court held that the sentencing judge was in the best position to explore and decide the factual issues of post-sentencing Tucker claims and that they should be resolved in the trial court. The court indicated that an appellate court could refrain from considering a Tucker claim until the sentencing court had an opportunity to resolve it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and remanded for resentencing.

People v. Kirtdoll


Docket No. 54,569


Supreme Court of Michigan


391 Mich. 370; 217 N.W.2d 37; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 141; 69 A.L.R.3d 1


November 9, 1973, Submitted  
April 16, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, Danhof, P. J., and Levin and Borradaile, JJ., reversing and remanding Recorder's Court of Detroit, Robert L. Evans, J.

 44 Mich App 237.
People v. Kirtdoll, 44 Mich. App. 237, 205 N.W.2d 44, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 1123 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Rape conviction reversed and robbery armed conviction affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of the judgment from the Court of Appeals, Division One (Michigan) that reversed the judgment from the trial court that had convicted defendant of rape and armed robbery and remanded for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction of rape and armed robbery on the basis that the introduction of the doctor's testimony was error and was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The main issue on appeal was whether the Michigan business entry statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2146 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.2146), authorized the admission into evidence of a hospital record in a criminal trial. In reversing the appellate court, the court overruled People v. Lewis, 293 N.W. 907 (Mich. 1940), which had held that the admission of such records in a criminal case without calling the maker thereof denied the accused his constitutional right to confront his accusers. The court determined that that case was correct in recognizing that there was a right to confrontation but was incorrect in treating the right of confrontation as absolute. Accordingly, the court held that records admissible in evidence under the business entry statute were admissible in criminal as well as civil cases. Therefore, the court held that the examining physician in the rape case was an appropriately indorsed witness and the prosecution did not exercise sufficient effort in producing him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court. The court reversed the rape conviction, but the robbery armed conviction was affirmed and defendant remained sentenced to a term of imprisonment from 15 to 30 years on the count of robbery armed.

Kropf v. Sterling Heights


Docket No. 54,184


Supreme Court of Michigan


391 Mich. 139; 215 N.W.2d 179; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 131


June 5, 1973, Submitted  
February 15, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 16, 1974.

 41 Mich App 21.
Kropf v. Sterling Heights, 41 Mich. App. 21, 199 N.W.2d 567, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 1275 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Michigan), which held that the city's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city challenged the judgment of a lower court which held that a city ordinance concerning zoning and land use was unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and reinstated and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court determined appellee builder-developer had failed to show that the zoning ordinance was unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious. Appellee was required to show that appellant, by its zoning ordinance, denied them substantive or procedural due process, equal protection of the laws, or deprived them of their property without just compensation. The court held that appellees did not allege, nor did their proof show, that they were denied procedural due process or that appellant had a policy of discriminating against multiple residences in order to raise an equal protection issue. The court concluded that appellees failed to prove that the zoning ordinance was unreasonable and that exclusion of other uses from the property was arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court judgment that found appellant city's zoning ordinance unconstitutional and reinstated the trial court judgment because appellee builder-developer failed to show that the ordinance was unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious.

People v. Burrill


Docket No. 54,788


Supreme Court of Michigan


391 Mich. 124; 214 N.W.2d 823; 1974 Mich. LEXIS 130


January 10, 1974, Submitted  
February 14, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kalamazoo, Raymond W. Fox, J., and from Court of Appeals prior to decision.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of an act of gross indecency with another male in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.338 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.570) by the trial court in Kalamazoo (Michigan). The Supreme Court of Michigan granted by-pass of the court of appeals.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that his conviction for gross indecency should have been set aside because the arrest warrant was issued on a complaint containing conclusory statements with no statement of underlying facts, the police officer who signed the complaint did not have personal knowledge of the facts and the magistrate did not examine witnesses having personal knowledge. A record was made which clearly established that the police officer that signed the complaint did not have personal knowledge of the commission of the offense. Nor did the magistrate examine any other witness before issuing the arrest warrant. The court held that, while the arrest warrant was indeed invalid because of the inadequacy of the allegations in the complaint, this did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction to try the offense charged in the information. To require in every case that the complainant and witnesses be examined first ex parte upon the filing of a complaint and again 12 days later at a preliminary examination would require a substantial enlargement of judicial and supporting personnel and would further inconvenience the victims of crime and other witnesses. The conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The conviction for gross indecency with another male was affirmed.

Quigley v. Dexter


Docket No. 54,561


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 707; 213 N.W.2d 166; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 173


November 6, 1973, Submitted  
December 18, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Lesinski, C. J., and Bronson and Targonski, JJ., affirming Washtenaw, Harold Van Domelen, J.

 43 Mich App 308.
Quigley v. Dexter, 43 Mich. App. 308, 204 N.W.2d 257, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 1032 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to circuit court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An individual filed an action against a township. After a decision by the township zoning board, an appeal was taken to the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Michigan). A review of that decision was put before the court.


OVERVIEW: In an action against a township, a decision was rendered by the zoning board of appeals. A review of the decision went before the circuit court. Upon review of the circuit court's decision, the court held that where zoning boards of appeals were established in a city, the decisions were final and the scope of review was essentially that formerly had by certiorari. Where zoning boards of appeals were established by townships, however, decisions were not final and were reviewed as to facts and law in the circuit court. The court held that the circuit court erroneously ruled that matters of discretion were properly vested in zoning boards. However, as the zoning board had been established by the township, the reviewing court was not limited to questions of law, but of facts also. Thus, the circuit judge should have treated the matter as a trial de novo and determined the proper order upon the merits of the cause of action. Thus, the court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision to the circuit court for a determination as to the merits of the cause.

Michigan Civil Rights Com. v. Clark


Docket Nos. 54,466, 54,467, 54,468


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 717; 212 N.W.2d 912; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 175


November 9, 1973, Submitted  
December 18, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, V. J. Brennan, P. J., and Quinn and O'Hara, JJ., affirming Wayne, Theodore R. Bohn, J., and Macomb, Alton H. Noe, J.

 42 Mich App 271.
Michigan Civil Rights Com. v. Clark, 42 Mich. App. 271, 201 N.W.2d 658, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 927 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to the circuit courts with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Civil Rights Commission (CRC) appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed the circuit courts' decisions that petitioner complainants could remove their CRC proceedings to the circuit courts.


OVERVIEW: Complaints were filed with the CRC concerning discrimination in the private rental and sale of housing. The complainants sought the removal of the CRC proceedings to the circuit court pursuant to § 401a of the Fair Housing Act of 1968, Mich. Comp. Laws § 564.401a. The petitions for removal were granted by the circuit courts. The CRC contended that it was obligated to investigate alleged discrimination and to secure the equal protection of civil rights. The court held that the "diminish-the-right" clause in the Mich. Const. art. V, § 29 (1963) did not create an automatic right to remove a proceeding from the jurisdiction of the CRC. Rather, the "diminish-the-right" clause assured persons against whom CRC proceedings were instituted that, despite the constitutional status of the CRC, they might have recourse to the courts of this state if the CRC proceeded in a manner justifying judicial intervention. Thus, it was not necessary to decide whether there was a civil right against discrimination in private rental and sale of housing. Section 401a of the Fair Housing Act of 1968 was unconstitutional as an unreasonable regulation of CRC procedures.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded to the circuit courts, with directions that they dismiss the complainants' petitions removing the CRC proceedings to those courts.

Production Steel Strip Corp. v. Detroit


Docket No. 54,428


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 508; 213 N.W.2d 419; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 158


June 6, 1973, Submitted

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant taxing authorities were granted leave to appeal a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division 1 (Michigan), which affirmed a judgment of the circuit court holding that plaintiff manufacturer was to be taxed on 1/2 month replenishment of stock from domestic sources.


OVERVIEW: The manufacturer's business, in part, was to purchase hot roll steel coils and by desclaing, cold reducing, annealing, and skin rolling, to produce cold roll strip of restricted tolerances and specialized steel finishes. On tax date, the manufacturer had at its plant enough steel coils to meet its needs for approximately two months. Other coils were stored in other locations close by where the coils would be easily moveable to the plant. The taxing authorities, who were local authorities who annually assessed, levied, and collected personal property taxes on such property as was within their corporate limits on the tax date, and the State Tax Commission made the assessment on the basis that a two and one-half month usage was essential to current requirements. The circuit court accepted the manufacturer's one-half month replenishment from domestic sources formula. The court held that the manufacturer had so acted upon the coils as to lose their distinctive character as imports. The court held that the State had a reasonable amount of latitude in determining what current operational needs of a taxpayer were, and the taxing authorities' judgment was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the circuit court for further proceedings.

GOVERNOR v. STATE TREASURER


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 389; 212 N.W.2d 711; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 152



December 14, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff governor inquired to the Supreme Court (Michigan) whether defendant state treasurer's school financing system denied students in school districts that had a relatively low state equalized value per pupil an equal educational opportunity.


OVERVIEW: Governor inquired to the court whether the Michigan school financing system substantially denied students an equal educational opportunity under the Equal Protection Clause of the Michigan Constitution or the 14th Amendment to the United States Constitution. The court held that state treasurer's financing system did not deny students in school districts having relatively low state equalized value per pupil an equal educational opportunity under Michigan's Equal Protection Clause. Furthermore, the state constitution did not prohibit a school district from levying taxes to support a level of expenditure for the education of students in the district beyond the level of expenditure in other districts, or oblige the legislature to supplement the revenues of other districts. Finally, the court answered negatively the question that raised a federal 14th Amendment claim.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint and vacated the opinions that had previously been entered.

People v. White


Docket No. 54,277


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 245; 212 N.W.2d 222; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 141


March 8, 1973, Submitted  
November 20, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, Levin, P. J., and Holbrook and Bronson, JJ., reversing Recorder's Court of Detroit, Robert E. DeMascio, J.

 41 Mich App 370.
People v. White, 41 Mich. App. 370, 200 N.W.2d 326, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 1329 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which reversed defendant's convictions for rape (Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.520 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.788)) and felonious assault (Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.82 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.277)) because defendant had already been convicted of kidnapping (Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.349 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.581)) as part of the same criminal transaction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant kidnapped, raped, and assaulted a woman. He was convicted of kidnapping in a trial court in one county, and he was convicted of rape and felonious assault in a different county. Defendant appealed his rape and felonious assault convictions. The appeals court reversed, holding that the "same transaction" test should have been followed in determining double jeopardy, and because defendant's crimes were all part of the same transaction, defendant should only have been tried once. The court affirmed. The court found that the three crimes committed by defendant were all part of a single criminal transaction, and the crimes were committed in a continuous time sequence and displayed a single intent and goal. The court adopted the same transaction test and held that defendant's second trial was improper and the resulting convictions on the charges of rape and felonious assault had to be reversed. The court found that the same transaction test was fair because the Michigan statutes creating jurisdiction did not preclude the use of the same transaction test and the prosecutor could have brought all of the charges against defendant in a single forum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals that reversed defendant's convictions.

People v. Blachura


Docket No. 54,133


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 326; 212 N.W.2d 182; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 145


May 9, 1973, Submitted  
November 20, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by People v. Blachura, 59 Mich. App. 664, 229 N.W.2d 877, 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1397 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Danhof, P. J., and Quinn and McGregor, JJ., granting leave to appeal from Oakland, Arthur E. Moore, J.
People v. Blachura, 388 Mich. 751, 1972 Mich. LEXIS 300 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Order granting leave to appeal to the Court of Appeals affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Michigan), which granted the People's request for emergency leave to appeal a decision of the trial court that ordered a new trial as to two counts of perjury against defendant and dismissed the remaining three counts after finding a violation of defendant's constitutional and statutory rights. Defendant argued that the appellate court lacked jurisdiction in the matter.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that Mich. Const. art. 6, § 10 provided that the jurisdiction of the court of appeals was to be provided by law. It also noted that, pursuant to that directive, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.308 was enacted providing in part for court of appeals jurisdiction over all final judgments. This obviously did not restrict the right of the People to appeal. Further, Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 806.2(2) (1963) gave the court of appeals the discretion to grant leave to appeal from any judgment, order, act, or failure to act by the circuit courts that was not a final judgment appealable as of right. This obviously did not restrict the right of the People to seek leave to appeal. Thus, the court concluded that the court of appeals had jurisdiction of the People's emergency appeal. It rejected defendant's argument that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 770.12 restricted the jurisdiction of the court of appeals, noting that this statute was passed and last amended long before the 1963 Michigan Constitution became effective bringing with it a new court, the court of appeals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' grant of leave to appeal in this case and remanded for a hearing on the merits.

W. A. FOOTE MEM. HOSP., INC. v. CITY OF JACKSON HOSP. AUTH.


Docket No. 54,017


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 193; 211 N.W.2d 649; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 139


June 5, 1973, Submitted  
October 17, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Jackson, Kevin J. Daley, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, city and hospital, appealed the decision of the Jackson County Circuit Court (Michigan), which granted summary judgment for intervenor attorney general in plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action against defendant hospital authority regarding 1969 Mich. Pub. Acts 38, the Hospital Finance Authority Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 331.31 et seq.; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 14.1220(1) et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, city and hospital, filed a complaint for a declaratory judgment to determine the constitutionality of 1969 Mich. Pub. Acts 38, the Hospital Finance Authority Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 331.31 et seq.; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 14.1220(1) et seq., and an order compelling defendant hospital authority to execute an agreement pursuant to Act 38. Intervenor attorney general filed a motion for summary judgment, which was granted. Plaintiffs appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision that Act 38 was constitutional because its objective of the improvement of health, welfare, and living conditions was constitutionally permissible and it did not violate the Michigan Constitution. The court held that plaintiff hospital could reorganize by using the provisions of Act 38 because it was a "hospital" within the meaning of that Act. Plaintiff city could transfer plaintiff hospital to defendant hospital authority pursuant to the reorganization agreement. The court also found that a charitable trust was not created by the individual who deeded the land to the city but ordered that the sale was subject to the determination of the heirs of the land donor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that trial court's decision that the Hospital Finance Authority Act was constitutional. The court reversed the judgment in favor of intervenor attorney general. Under the Hospital Finance Authority Act, plaintiff city could transfer plaintiff hospital to defendant hospital authority because plaintiff hospital was a "hospital" within the meaning of the act. The case was remanded for a determination of heirs of the land's donor.

In re Advisory Opinion etc.


Docket Nos. 54,722, 54,723


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 166; 211 N.W.2d 28; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 179


Submitted May 18, 1973. No. 17 May Term 1973  
Statutes declared unconstitutional in part and constitutional in part October 17, 1973.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state senate requested the opinion of the court as to the constitutionality of a plan for state borrowing to establish a fund for loans to school districts and as to the applicability of the 15 mill limitations on an ad valorem tax to pay notes or bonds issued to fund present or projected operating deficits of a school district.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the state senate's request for an advisory opinion on the constitutionality of legislation. The court held that the plan for state borrowing to establish a fund for loans to school districts created a debt within the constitutional proscription against the issuance of any evidence of state indebtedness except for debts authorized pursuant to the constitution even though the loans contemplated to the state treasurer and by him to the school district had been structured so that the indebtedness would not be repaid by the people of the state at large but primarily by residents of the school district. The court held that the constitutional provision that ad valorem taxes imposed upon real and personal property in any one year should not exceed 15 mills unless approved by a vote of the electors did not apply to the funding of accumulated operating deficits in school districts, and a non-voted millage could be levied to pay the principal and interest on bonds issued to fund present or projected operating deficits. The court rendered an opinion declaring the statutes unconstitutional in part and constitutional in part.


OUTCOME: The court rendered an advisory opinion on the constitutionality of legislation as requested by the state senate. The court declared the statutes unconstitutional in part and constitutional in part.

Carver v. McKernan


Docket No. 54,371


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 96; 211 N.W.2d 24; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 135


January 3, 1973, Submitted  
October 17, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Joseph G. Rashid, J., and from Court of Appeals prior to decision.
Carver v. McKernan, 388 Mich. 781, 1972 Mich. LEXIS 403 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victims appealed an order of the trial court (Michigan), which granted defendant Secretary of State's motion for accelerated judgment on the basis of the victims' failure to give notice of intent to claim against the Motor Vehicle Accident Claim Fund within six months of the accrual of the cause of action. The trial court ruled that notice to the Secretary as required by statute was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The accident victims had filed a claim with the car owner's insurance carrier, but brought the action against the owner and the Secretary of State when the insurer denied coverage because the car was not driven with consent of the owner. The accident victims contended that the notice requirements of the Motor Vehicle Claims Act (Act), 1965 Mich. Pub. Acts 198, § 18, was unconstitutional as violative of the due process and equal protection provisions of the federal and state constitutions. The court granted bypass of the court of appeals because of its conviction that the validity of the notice requirements presented a recurring problem in the administration of the Act. The court acknowledged that statutes that limited access to the courts by people seeking redress for wrongs were disfavored. However, having concluded that there was a legitimate purpose for the notice provision in an earlier case, the court was constrained to hold that the notice provision did not necessarily violate the constitution. Nonetheless, the court held that only upon a showing of prejudice by the Secretary from the failure to give the notice required by the Act could a claim against the fund be dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court's order of dismissal, reinstated the claim against the fund, and remanded the matter for further proceedings pursuant to the court's opinion.

People v. Chism


Docket No. 53,409


Supreme Court of Michigan


390 Mich. 104; 211 N.W.2d 193; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 136


January 4, 1973, Submitted

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Michigan Court of Appeals that upheld his first-degree murder conviction and the trial court's denial of his motions to dismiss on speedy trial grounds and to suppress evidence discovered in his home after he and his wife gave written consent to search.


OVERVIEW: After a woman was killed by a letter bomb, police went to defendant's home, advised him of his Miranda rights, and obtained written consent from him and his wife to a search of their home, during which certain evidence seized. Defendant was found guilty and his conviction was upheld by the appellate court. On further review, the court ruled that the responsibility for the long pretrial delay lay with defendant due to his appeal and need for preparation and he failed to show prejudice from the delay. The evidence of the lye pills was admissible to show intent to kill and valid consent for the search was clearly shown.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

PALEY v. COCA COLA CO.


Docket No. 54,058


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 583; 209 N.W.2d 232; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 119


March 6, 1973, Submitted  
July 24, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, Levin, P. J., and Danhof and O'Hara, JJ., reversing and remanding Oakland, Robert L. Templin, J.

 39 Mich App 379.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed by an equally divided Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class of consumers (class) filed a class action against defendant soft drink company and contest creator (company) for unfair trade practices, breach of contract, and fraudulent misrepresentations. The trial court granted the company's motion to dismiss, summary judgment, and accelerated judgments. The Court of Appeals (Michigan) vacated the trial court judgment and remanded and the court granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The action arose after the company created and conducted a nationwide contest by distributing cards with 10 questions. The answers were to have been found on soft drink bottle tops and cartons. At the last minute after most contestants filed their answers new rules were announced indicating some questions required two answers. The change in the contest rules prevented many contestants from winning. The court had to determine if the circuit court under Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.606 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.605) or the district court under Mich. Comp. Law § 600.8301 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.8301) had jurisdiction over the controversy. The court determined that a class action was historically equitable in nature within the meaning of Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.8315 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.8315). The court then determined whether the circuit court was divested of class actions. The court concluded that there was a presumption against divestiture of court jurisdiction plus the limitation under § 8315 indicated a legislative intent not to divest the circuit courts of class action jurisdiction. Therefore, the circuit court was the only one in which a class action could have been maintained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Michigan Consol. Gas Co. v. Michigan Public Service Com.

389 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. McFarlin


Docket Nos. 54,201, 54,211, 54,197


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 557; 208 N.W.2d 504; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 118; 64 A.L.R.3d 1274


April 5, 1973, Submitted  
June 28, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Lesinski, C. J., and Bronson and Targonski, JJ., reversing and remanding Genesee, John W. Baker, J.

 41 Mich App 116.

Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Lesinski, C. J., and Bronson and Targonski, JJ., reversing and remanding Genesee, Anthony J. Mansour, J.

Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Quinn, P. J., and Fitzgerald and Van Valkenburg, JJ., affirming Washtenaw, Ross W. Campbell, J.
People v. McFarlin, 41 Mich. App. 116, 199 N.W.2d 684, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 1290 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Reversed. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed the judgment from the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Michigan), which reversed two defendants' felony convictions and prison sentences and remanded after holding that a judge could not consider an adult offender's juvenile offense record as a factor in imposing a sentence. In a consolidated case, defendant appealed the judgment that affirmed his felony conviction and prison sentence.


OVERVIEW: All three defendants were convicted of felonies and sentenced to prison terms. After the appellate court held that a judge could not consider an adult offender's juvenile offense record in imposing a sentence, reversed two defendants' convictions, and remanded, the people appealed. In the third case, defendant appealed his conviction. The court reversed for two defendants and affirmed for the third. The presentence report for an adult offender had to include information concerning juvenile history, including a disposition by a juvenile court. It was proper for the courts to consider this information as a factor in sentencing adult offenders. The sentence had to be tailored to the particular circumstances of the case and the offender in an effort to balance both society's need for protection and its interest in maximizing the offender's rehabilitative potential. A judge needed complete information to set a proper individualized sentence. A juvenile court history could reveal a pattern of lawbreaking and the offender's response to previous rehabilitative efforts. Information about social or family difficulties and other facts were essential to an informed sentencing decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court that reversed two defendants' felony convictions and prison sentences. The court affirmed the judgment that affirmed the third defendant's conviction and prison sentence.

People v. Wolff


Docket No. 53,896


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 398; 208 N.W.2d 457; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 112


January 4, 1973, Submitted  
June 18, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, V. J. Brennan, P. J., and Levin and Targonski, JJ., denying application for leave to appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, Elvin L. Davenport, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Michigan Court of Appeals that denied his application for leave to appeal from the judgment of his conviction for armed robbery, which was entered after the trial court sua sponte vacated defendant's previously accepted guilty plea to unarmed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with armed robbery. He entered a guilty plea to unarmed robbery and his plea was accepted by the trial court. Before sentencing, however, the trial court vacated the plea because defendant had protested his innocence in a pre-sentencing report. He was subsequently found guilty of armed robbery and the court of appeals rejected his appeal. In reversing, the supreme court ruled that defendant's guilty plea to the lesser-offense of unarmed robbery was properly accepted by the trial court after the colloquy required by Mich. Comp. Laws § 768.35 and it was reversible error to set that plea aside against defendant's wishes. Although § 768.35 required that the trial judge satisfy himself that there was a factual basis for the plea, doubt as to guilt did not preclude such a plea because an accused could protest his innocence altogether and still offer to plead guilty intelligently, deliberately, and freely.


OUTCOME: The conviction for armed robbery was reversed, the order vacating the plea of guilty to unarmed robbery was set aside, the plea of guilty thereto was reinstated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on that offense.

Advisory Opinion re Constitutionality of 1972 PA 294


Docket No. 54,503


SUPREME COURT OF MICHIGAN


389 Mich. 441; 208 N.W.2d 469; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 180


Submitted March 9, 1973. (No. 16 March Term 1973)  
Statute declared constitutional June 18, 1973 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The governor and the senate requested an advisory opinion from the court on the constitutionality of 1972 Mich. Pub. Acts 294, which added chapter 31 to the Insurance Code of 1956. The court granted the requests with respect to a total of three questions, which asked whether the Act violated Mich. Const. art. 4, §§ 24 and 25, and whether two phrases as used in § 3135 of the Act were "sufficient for legal interpretation."


OVERVIEW: The court first noted that Mich. Const. art. 3, § 8 provided that either house of the legislature or the governor could request the opinion of the Michigan Supreme Court on important questions of law. It emphasized that an advisory opinion did not constitute a decision of the court and was not precedentially binding in the same sense as a decision of the court after a hearing on the merits. The court then determined that the Act complied with Mich. Const. art. 4, § 24 because the Act embraced only one subject which was the Insurance Code. The court observed that the provision was designed mainly to prevent the legislature from passing laws not fully understood. In holding that the Act did not violate Mich. Const. art. 4, § 25, which stated that no law shall be revised, altered, or amended by reference to its title only, the court concluded that the Act detailed all that was required for institution of a "no-fault" system of motor vehicle insurance. It was an act complete within itself. The court finally determined that the phrases "serious impairment of body function" and "permanent serious disfigurement" provided standards sufficient for legal interpretation.


OUTCOME: The court held that the Act embraced only one subject, the enactment standard had been met, and the Act was complete within itself. It was, therefore, constitutional.

People v. Bricker


Docket No. 54,434


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 524; 208 N.W.2d 172; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 114


April 2, 1973, Submitted  
June 18, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, Danhof, P.J., and T.M. Burns and Van Valkenburg, JJ., affirming Oakland, Frederick C. Ziem, J.

 42 Mich App 352.
People v. Bricker, 42 Mich. App. 352, 201 N.W.2d 647, 1972 Mich. App. LEXIS 940 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a non-physician, appealed from the order of the Michigan Court of Appeals, Division 2, which affirmed the trial court's judgment, convicting defendant, upon a jury verdict, of conspiracy (Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 740.157a) to commit an abortion (Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.14), and which sentenced him to one to four years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant based his appeal on the decisions of the U.S. Supreme Court in Roe v. Wade and Doe v. Bolton, which held that certain state criminal abortion statutes were unconstitutional. The court held that, under the Supremacy Clause, it was bound by those decisions and that Michigan's criminal abortion statute could not stand as relating to abortions in the first trimester of a pregnancy as authorized by the pregnant woman's attending physician in the exercise of his medical judgment. However, defendant was not a licensed physician. The court found that the exception required by the Supreme Court in Roe v. Wade could properly be read into the Michigan criminal abortion statutes to preserve their constitutionality. It then upheld defendant's conviction, finding that the excision from the statute, by constitutional construction, of a certain class, viz. medical professionals, neither affected the balance of the classes coming within the ambit of the clear legislative intent to proscribe abortion nor exonerated the same from criminal responsibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Larkin v. Wayne Prosecutor


Docket No. 54,438


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 533; 208 N.W.2d 176; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 115


April 2, 1973, Submitted  
June 18, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Charles Kaufman, J., and from Court of Appeals prior to decision.
Larkin v. Wayne, 388 Mich. 788, 1972 Mich. LEXIS 725 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted leave to appeal from a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Wayne County (Michigan), which granted plaintiff physicians declaratory and injunctive relief in their actions against defendant prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court granted the physicians' request for declaratory and injunctive relief in their action against the prosecutor. The court, sua sponte, granted leave to appeal and stayed the circuit court's decision. The court refused to issue an injunction. It addressed the impact of recent United States Supreme Court decisions on various Michigan statutes that governed the availability of abortion. The court found that Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.15 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.205), which made illegal the selling of drugs intended to procure an abortion, was constitutional. It also found that the scope of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.322 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.554) was limited to abortions caused by a felonious assault upon the mother. Moreover, the word "child" as used in that provision and Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.323 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.555), which made illegal the destruction of a "quick child," referred to a viable child in its mother's womb. Furthermore, procuring a criminal abortion and aiding and abetting such activity remained unlawful conduct that was punishable under Mich. Comp. Laws § 338.53 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 14.533) and Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.323 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.555).


OUTCOME: The court issued a declaratory judgment, which discussed the constitutionality of various Michigan statutes that addressed the issue of abortion. The court did not issue an injunctive in light of the declaratory relief it had granted. No costs were assessed.

YOUNG v. DETROIT CITY CLERK

Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 333; 207 N.W.2d 126; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 108

May 10, 1973, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate obtained emergency bypass leave for review of a decision from the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which dismissed his complaint that appellee city clerk had improperly applied Mich. Const. art 4, § 9, to bar the candidate from running for mayoral office because he was an incumbent state senator.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was a state senator who wanted to run for the office of the Mayor of Detroit. The city clerk rejected the nominating petitions and a filing fee because Mich. Const. art 4, § 9, prohibited dual office. The trial court dismissed the candidate's action for mandamus relief. On appeal, the court granted emergency bypass relief, reversed the decision of the trial court, and directed issuance of the requested writ because the office of the Mayor of the City of Detroit was a local office and not a state office and art 4, § 9, was not a bar to the candidate from being a candidate in a mayoral primary election, notwithstanding some cases that held to the contrary, which were expressly overruled. The court held that a prior case that involved the same candidate was not res judicata of the issue presented because the applicable legal context had changed and it would be inequitable to preclude a determination in the new case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for the issuance of the writ of mandamus as requested.

People v. Adams


Docket No. 53,562


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 222; 205 N.W.2d 415; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 100; 59 A.L.R.3d 1288


March 9, 1972, Submitted  
March 27, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 18, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 2, J. H. Gillis, P. J., and Bronson and Levin, JJ., reversing Jackson, Charles J. Falahee, J.

 34 Mich App 546.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Michigan), reversing defendant's conviction for kidnapping under Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.349.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with other prison inmates, seized a prison guard at knife point and threatened to kill the guard. Defendant and the other inmates moved the guard from a cell block to the prison hospital. The guard was eventually released unharmed, and the inmates' weapons were surrendered. Defendant was convicted of kidnapping by a jury. The court of appeals reversed the conviction, finding there was no asportation and therefore no kidnapping. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction in the trial court and affirmed the court of appeals' decision in part, reversed in part, and remanded. The court held that the Michigan kidnapping statute was unconstitutional as being overbroad without the interpolation of the concept of asportation. The court concluded that the asportation necessary to sustain a conviction for kidnapping must not be merely incidental to the commission of a lesser underlying crime, but must be incidental to the commission of the kidnapping itself. The court determined that it was for the jury to decide whether the necessary asportation was present, and the trial court had erred in failing to charge the jury as to the question of asportation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the conviction in the trial court, and affirmed the decision of the court of appeals in part, reversed it in part, and remanded the matter back to the trial court.

West Shore Community College v. Manistee County Board of Comm'rs


Docket Nos. 53,910, 53,911


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 287; 205 N.W.2d 441; 1973 Mich. LEXIS 104


January 3, 1973, Submitted  
March 27, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Manistee, Charles A. Wickens, J., and from Court of Appeals prior to decision.
W. Shore Cmty. College v. Manistee County Bd. of Comm'Rs, 386 Mich. 791, 1972 Mich. LEXIS 280 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In its suit against defendant county board of commissioners, plaintiff community college sought a declaration that it was entitled to levy three-tenths of one mill in ad valorem taxes to pay debt service and to an injunction restraining the board from spreading taxes without including the requested three-tenths of one mill. The Circuit Court, Manistee County (Michigan) declined to grant the relief requested. The college appealed.


OVERVIEW: The community college sought a declaration that it was entitled to levy three-tenths of one mill in ad valorem taxes to pay debt service and sought an injunction restraining the county board of commissioners from spreading taxes without including the requested three-tenths of one mill. The college argued that it was authorized to levy ad valorem taxes without limitation as to rate or amount for the purpose of paying the debt service upon its outstanding bonded indebtedness. The college also argued that the board had a duty to spread such taxes upon the request of the college board of trustees and that no vote of the people was necessary to authorize such taxes. The trial court declined to grant the relief requested by the college. On appeal, the court remanded the case for a new trial. The court found that, although certain factors raised some question as to the propriety of imposing the three-tenths mill over-levy, the factors, in the absence of further proofs, did not preponderate in favor of the board. According to the court, on remand, the board had the burden of proving that the levy was not in fact imposed for the payment of debt service.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision denying the community college's request for a declaration that it was entitled to levy .3 of one mill in ad valorem taxes to pay debt service and for an injunction restraining the county board of commissioners from spreading taxes without including the requested .3 of one mill. The matter was remanded for a new trial.

 

397 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


GOVERNOR v. STATE TREASURER


Docket No. 53,809


Supreme Court of Michigan


389 Mich. 1; 203 N.W.2d 457; 1972 Mich. LEXIS 150


June 6, 1972, Submitted  
December 29, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted January 30, 1973. Opinions Vacated December 14, 1973, see 390 Mich   .


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified questions from Ingham, Sam Street Hughes, J.



DISPOSITION: Question answered favorably to plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state officials filed a complaint with the Ingham County Circuit Court (Michigan), in which certain public school parents joined, seeking a declaratory judgment that the Michigan public school financing system violated the equal protection of laws guaranteed in Mich. Const. art. I, § 2. The circuit court then certified the constitutional question to the court.


OVERVIEW: The Michigan school system was financed with a combination of local property taxes and state school aid appropriations. Plaintiff state officials sought a declaratory judgment that the system was unconstitutional, resulting in disparities in per pupil spending such that wealthier school districts were able to spend more per pupil than poorer districts. Plaintiffs, including parents who intervened, contended that the system violated equal protection guarantees provided for in the Mich. Const. art. I, § 2. The circuit court certified the constitutional question to the court. The court held that the financing system denied equal protection. The court held that education was a fundamental interest. The court held that the desire of achieving some local control over school districts was not a compelling state interest in light of the fact that the school system was state run and the only local control was the right to increase local property taxes. The court also held that, even if education was not a fundamental interest, the system failed to pass the less onerous test of whether there was a rational relationship between the system and the interest to assert local control.


OUTCOME: The court held that the state public school financing system denied equal protection of the laws guaranteed by the Michigan Constitution when measured by both the "compelling state interest" and the "rational" classification tests.

 

398 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


GALLEGOS v. GLASER CRANDELL CO.


Docket No. 53,541


Supreme Court of Michigan


388 Mich. 654; 202 N.W.2d 786; 1972 Mich. LEXIS 143


April 5, 1972, Submitted  
December 21, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 3, R.B. Burns, P.J., and Fitzgerald and J.H. Gillis, J.J., affirming Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.

 34 Mich App 489.
Gallegos v. Glaser Crandell Co., 34 Mich. App. 489, 192 N.W.2d 52, 1971 Mich. App. LEXIS 1637 (1971)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded to Workmen's Compensation Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees sought review of a judgment by the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which ruled in favor of defendant employer and affirmed the decision of the workmen's compensation appeal board (board), which had denied benefits to the employees for injuries that arose in the course of their employment.


OVERVIEW: The employees were seasonal workers who performed manual labor on the employer's farm. The employees sustained injuries during their employment and applied for workmen's compensation benefits. The board denied the employees' claim. The appellate court affirmed the board's decision stating that the employees were exempt from coverage under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.111 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.237(111)) because they were piecework employees or did not work 35 hours per week for the employer for 13 or more consecutive weeks. On appeal the court reversed and remanded the appellate court's decision. The court held that those portions of the statute excepting piecework and seasonal employees were unconstitutional. The court noted that the classification was limited by race as it was largely composed of minorities. Such classifications were inherently suspect and could be sustained only on a showing of a compelling government interest. No compelling government interest was shown that justified the exclusion of the employees from workmen's compensation, and the statute was therefore a violation of the employees' equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court exempting the employees from workmen's compensation and remanded the case to the workmen's compensation commission for determination of the claim.

 

399 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Collins


Docket No. 53,761


Supreme Court of Michigan


388 Mich. 680; 202 N.W.2d 769; 1972 Mich. LEXIS 144


October 3, 1972, Submitted  
December 21, 1972, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, Levin, P. J., and Quinn and V. J. Brennan, JJ., affirming Recorder's Court of Detroit, George W. Crockett, Jr., J.

 36 Mich App 400.
People v. Collins, 36 Mich. App. 400, 194 N.W.2d 131, 1971 Mich. App. LEXIS 1323 (1971)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a decision of the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which affirmed his conviction for armed robbery entered in the trial court. Defendant specifically challenged the denial of his motion to dismiss the charge against him for failure to grant him a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that both the trial court and the lower court erred by denying his motion to dismiss the armed robbery charge for failure to grant him a speedy trial. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and noted that the delay, although unduly long, was not long enough to presume prejudice. The court then applied the balancing test found in Barker v. Wingo 407 U.S. 514, 33 L. Ed. 2d (1972) to defendant's case. The court pointed out that the delay itself was unduly long unless the other factors articulated in the Barker case required a different result. The court then determined that the reasons for the delay were as much the fault of defendant as they were the fault of the state. The court noted that defendant was out of jail during much of this time. The court also pointed out that defendant did not assert his right to a speedy trial until the day before his trial began. Again, the court noted that defendant was unconcerned about the trial while he was out on bail. Finally, the court noted that defendant failed to sufficiently establish that the delay had prejudiced his defense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision affirming the defendant's conviction.

 

400 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Smigel v. Southgate Community School Dist.


Docket No. 53,008


Supreme Court of Michigan


388 Mich. 531; 202 N.W.2d 305; 1972 Mich. LEXIS 135; 81 L.R.R.M. 2944


September 17, 1971, Submitted  
November 29, 1972, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 30, 1973.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Appeals, Division 1, Quinn, P.J., and J.H. Gillis and O'Hara, JJ., reversing and remanding Wayne, Thomas J. Foley, J.

 24 Mich App 179.
Smigel v. Southgate Community School Dist., 24 Mich. App. 179, 180 N.W.2d 215, 1970 Mich. App. LEXIS 1675 (1970)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the order from the Court of Appeals (Michigan), which denied injunctive relief in their challenge to an "agency shop" provision in a collective bargaining agreement approved by defendant employer.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sought injunctive relief in their challenge to an "agency shop" provision in a collective bargaining agreement imposing a payroll deduction for non-union members as violative of the prohibition of activities that either encourage or discourage union membership in Mich. Comp. Laws. § 423.210, Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.455(10). The court reversed the denial of the injunction and remanded the case for imposition of the injunction. The court held that the agreement made no effort to relate the nonmembers' economic obligations to actual collective bargaining expenses and, thus, was prohibited. The court remanded for imposition of the injunction and held that there was no need for proof of de facto discrimination because there was de jure discrimination of a magnitude sufficient to invalidate the clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the case to the trial court for the entry of injunctive relief.
